On the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter XXXVIII.
When the patient does not obey the instructions for section and treatment that we have described in its place, and is frightened by it, perhaps he will heal with a cauterization.
When a fistula therefore occurs in someone and becomes chronic, pus runs from it, and corrupt humors (fluids) gather. Therefore, with due care, one should explore it with a delicate probe. Then, determine the depth of it with the probe.
Then apply the cautery, which is similar to a hot iron. Then insert the burning instrument itself into the fistula, and determine how far the clot (or blockage) has entered.
And apply the cautery repeatedly over it until all those corrupt bodies are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to your need.
And guard yourself from the burn of nerve, if it is there, or a large vein; or if the fistula extends to the urinary body, or to the intestinal body, then guard yourself from all these places.
And do not perform it unless there is a fistula in a fleshy part, for you think that it does not penetrate.
Then pay attention to the place until it heals.
If, however, the place is sealed and the materials are removed from it, and it remains like that for a long time, then you know that it has already healed completely.
And if the materials do not separate from it, then know that it is penetrating, or there is a deep hole corrupted within it, or as if it were among those, whose memory will come to its place.
§ On the method of cauterizing veins.
When there is pain in the kidneys due to cold or excessive heat, and they are weakened because of it, then one should cauterize them immediately over a hot stone placed on top of the kidneys, with a cautery iron over every kidney, whose memory precedes it.
And perhaps we cauterize it again a second time in the same hot stone. That is why three lines will come. Therefore they will be the last resort in treatment.
Regarding the cauterization of vesicles.
When weakness and softening due to cold and moistures occur in the vesicle, until the patient is unable to retain urine, then cauterize it at the lower part of the suprarrenal gland above the vesicle, where the hairs begin to grow, and use a cauterizer from above and another from below; and the length of this cauterization should be according to the size of the thumb: and cauterize it also with a cauterizer on the lower back, or with two cauterizers if needed; and let it follow the same procedure as before.
Regarding the method of cauterization of the matrix.
When cold and moistures affect the matrix, preventing conception and causing irregular menstruation, with pain upon their onset, then it should be cauterized with three cauterizers around the navel, as we mentioned in the cauterization of the vesicle, and with a cauterizer above the lower back or with two cauterizers; and let it follow the same procedure as before.
On the method of cauterization for a dislocated joint.
When the humidities of the mucous membranes are discharged into the anchor (joint), they become the cause of its exit from its place; and this is indicated by the extension of one leg over the other when they are compared again: and the site of dislocation is found to be hollow in it.
Therefore, it is necessary to cauterize the infirm joint above the anchor with a similar circular cautery; after you have marked with wax around the joints, as it were, and so that the joint itself falls into the middle of the circle.
If this cautery is not present for you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, using a large oily cautery; and make the depth of the cautery according to the thickness of the skin throughout.
Then take care of it until it is healed.
**On the method of cauterization for sciatica.**
When pain occurs in the ankle joint due to cold and moisture, and this treatment does not improve but instead aggravates the condition, then it is necessary to relieve the patient from thick humours with foul or artificial pills, and similar remedies. Then apply a cauterization.
The method of cauterization is in this case according to two methods: either a cautery with medicated ointments or a cautery with fire.
A cautery with fire is according to many methods.
One of these methods involves cauterizing the ankle joint itself with three triangular cautery instruments, in this form. And make them a deep incision, good or bad. And leave a space between each cautery that is the width of a finger; and the cautery should be oiled.
However, a cautery is also made in the middle on top of the ankle joint itself. Why are there four cauterizations?
And if you cauterize with a circle, whose shape precedes in the cauterization of the dislocation of the ankle, it should be so that the circle contains the ankle completely.
And burn the thickening of the skin throughout.
This is the method of cauterization in sciatica when the pain is adhering to the ankle itself and does not extend to the hip and leg.
However, if it extends to the hip and leg, then cauterize the inside of the hip with two cauterizations, on the spot where the patient feels pain, and use your cautery on the four fingers towards the outer part a little bit: and let the cauterization be surgical.
And the depth of the cauterization should be according to the depth of the thickening of the skin.
If the patient feels that the pain extends almost to the toes, then cauterize the place indicated by the patient with a point, three, four, or more cauteries if needed.
And if he indicates that the pain is under the knee towards the leg, then cauterize the place with a single cautery of the knife.
And be careful in all your cauterizations so as not to burn the last nerves or a large artery, and take care through it to avoid further harm or contraction of the afflicted part.
And I have indeed seen one and another of those who cauterized on the wound, and ended up with cauterization, and the foot was inflated, until the swelling reached the toe, and it was entirely perforated and corrupted; then there was a rupture of the abdomen, and death followed afterwards.
If there is pain in both parts at the same time, cauterize both according to this manner.
And certain wise ones spoke about cauterizing the aching part, whose cauterization is this method. Make a similar one from iron, whose diameter is the middle of the palm: and it should be near the opening according to the thickness of the finger's nucleus, or a little less; and within that same third should be placed.
And let the space between each pin be the length of a thumb; and let the pins be open from both parts; and their height should be like a node, or two nodes; and make handles for them out of well-suited iron within the pins.
Then it is heated over fire until it glows, and scatters sparks; then place it on the scales above the infected foot lying on its healthy side. Therefore, cauterize him with three round cauterizations using one application of heat.
Then leave it for three days. After that, apply poultices with butter, and leave the open wound for many days. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Albucasis says that with this kind of cauterization, we have little experience because of the fear it inspires and because few people know how to perform it.
Nevertheless, for those who endure it, there is good healing, and they will find its place.
When cauterization is performed alongside medicines, as you do with two identical tools having a perforated ring, into which descends the hinge of its door made of iron or bronze, whose length reaches the wall—with two knots, or something like them, at their top—...
And there should be a space between both, equal to the thickness of a finger, open below and above, and such that they fit together in this way.
Then place it on the patient's healthy side, lying on their sick side. And press your hand firmly over the wound. Then apply a poultice between two circles of hot water, heated with fire to the point of warmth, and hold it for an appropriate amount of time; thus the patient will tolerate both the biting (of the wound) and its burning, as he himself caused the bite like fire until it subsides.
Then raise your hand with the instrument and wipe away the hot water from the wound with sweet water entirely; then leave it for three days.
And place butter over it until the burn's blackness is removed; and leave it for several days, and pus will flow from it. It is indeed the last resort in healing.
Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
If the pain extends to the thigh or the foot, make a soak for him according to what you did for the wound, equally containing water.
And this is the way of hot water, and I have already written about it in the book on medical rectification. Take some alkali and unextinguished lime, of each one part; rub both, and put them in a new pot, whose lower part is perforated with a small hole according to the quantity that will enter it; and place beneath the bottom of the pot another pot that has been previously hollowed out: then throw over the alkali and lime water from a sweet spring, so that both are submerged by one finger; after which compress them well with your hand, and leave the pot until sharp water descends to the lower part of the hollowed-out pot.
Then add all that water to it and throw it over another lime; and continue until it renews itself.
For at that time it will be very sharp and effective, which is administered in many medical operations, and in the cauterization of the other parts of the body. Because it performs the operation of fire itself.
And there are medicines with which wide burns are cauterized, such as pitch, turpentine, and almond oil, and lime with soap, so that each is mixed together.
And Galen indeed reported, narrating the cure of a certain man from ancient times who was cured of the pain of the ankle and sciatic nerve, and he praised it as being very magnificent. And he said that it did not need any other treatment, and that he was healed at once, until he returned, because perhaps he had entered the bath with a disease, and left it already healthy.
And it is taken from a green vegetable; if it cannot be found fresh, it is taken dry and recent; and it is heated much with some fat, and placed on the spot where there is pain, in the leg or hip, and bound, and left for three hours' duration, or according to the amount that the patient feels relief from the heat. Then insert it into the bath.
When the body becomes cold, insert it into the fire. Since the pain retreats, it is healed.
And know this, for it is not necessary that anyone use a cauterizing iron with these medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides, who said that goat dung, when applied with it to a sciatic vein, relieves him; and the cauterization is made in this way. Take the wool, and soak it in old oil, and place it on the deep spot that is between the big toe of the foot and the ankle, and closer to the ankle.
Then take dry goat dung, and ignite it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it upon the wound and release it until it heals. Then repeat this process. Therefore continue this until sensation returns to the midpoint, and the pain ceases.
And this method of burning is called the vaccinating burn.
§ On the burning of the back's pain.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back from many causes, or from chance, or from a blow, or from excessive evacuation, and similar conditions due to the injection of cold and moist material; and the cauterizing does not take place unless it is in this particular case alone which is caused by the injection of cold material.
Therefore after evacuation of the infirmity with foul pills and similar ones, three lines should be drawn on the back where there is pain according to its width, then signs with encaustic are made in every line five times or more punctures, according to the quantity which came from the tolerance of the nurse, and the cauterization is done when the cauterizing point has been reached.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauterizations, using a cautery on the mid-clasp, in this manner.
**On the manner of cauterization in incipient gangrene.**
This illness often occurs in very young children.
And the sign of its onset in children is: that a constriction occurs above the belly during breathing, and movement; and you will find it in the lower spine and the knots of his back, which have already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When you see this, and wish to do it, then cauterize the same with a circular cautery in this form.
And the cautery should take hold over all parts of the vertebrae equally: and if you wish to cauterize around the vertebrae with a point cautery, make two or three lines, and the points should be close together.
Then take care of the place until it heals as we said.
And beware, do not apply cauterization to the gangrene that occurs from nerve spasm.
On the method of cauterizing podagra and pained joints.
When the pains of the joined parts are caused by cold humidities that extend to any part of the body, and when pains occur in the feet, it is customarily called podagra by physicians.
When podagra is cured by means of treatment due to cold causes and the pains do not subside, then cautery should be used to remove them.
And it is done that after evacuating the joint of the foot, cautery should be applied with many cauteries and this cautery is with oil.
And if you need to make points on the surface of the foot, then make them with a cautery point. If the pains rise up to the knees or other joints, and this happens often, then cauterize the whole knee with three cauteries or four from every side, using the same cautery as for the claw.
However, if more of this cautery is necessary for you, then cauterize the whole thing. And do not immerse your hand with a cautery, but rather place it around the thickness of the skin only.
However, if the pains rise to the knees and back, then administer what we said regarding cautery in its chapter.
If the pains are only in the hands, then make dots around with a flame, as two lines are resolved.
However, if there remains pain in the fingers, then make dots on them, over every knot and also on the palm of the hand.
However, if the pains rise after days to the forearms or shoulders, then cauterize both from every part.
And do not delay the weak from good treatment, from receiving medicines. For if a good treatment is done, and the phlegm is expelled, it will be healed with God's help through this cautery.
**On the method of cauterization in ruptures.**
When a rupture occurs in the groin and the intestine descends towards the testicle, becoming inflamed, it is then necessary to urge the patient to abstain from food on that day. And it should be used to release the stool from its lower part.
Then he should sit between your hands on his back and urge him to hold his breath until he expulses the stool or the intestine.
Then reduce the swelling with your fingers and mark with a hot wax sigil above the rupture on the ribcage, where the end of the sigil is similar to the midpoint of a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then apply a hot iron whose shape is as described until it turns white and releases the pus. Then reduce the intestine or the hernia to its cavity. Then the assistant should place his hand over the area to prevent the intestine from escaping and you, having already opened between the patient's legs, placed a poultice beneath and another above his groin, and another one over his chest which holds the hands in place.
Then place the hot iron over the sigil, with your hand holding the cautery straight. And hold it yourself, until you gain access to the mouth with it; or use it again once with another if you have not gained access to the mouth with it at first up to the end of the jaw.
And be careful to observe the exit of the intestine during your cauterization, so as not to burn it itself, and let it heal through that onto the afflicted part or cause great pain or death.
And know that when you do not gain access to the mouth with your cautery, your operation is in vain.
And it is necessary that the cautery for children be subtle, according to their measure.
Then take care with the remaining ointments until it heals.
And the afflicted person should lie on their back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you provide its nourishment for the duration of its healing, which softens its bowels; so that the intestine does not come out near the anus and expulsion.
Then when you want to rise after forty days, then administer a well-made ligature and hold it for another forty days.
And it becomes lessened by labour, and filling with food and drink, and restless conversations.
For when this regimen is used, thus is achieved complete healing.
And I will speak of the healing of ruptures with incisions in its chapter.
When ruptures occur in the rest of the stomach, and they are beginning and appear not to be spreading, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size; and it should be treated from then on as if it were one-third of it. Then attend to it yourself, as we said, and let it not be added.
And some have said that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery in this form.
After it is sealed with wax, a line is drawn which crosses the width at the upper side of the rupture, and another line at the lower side. And place your hand in the middle with the cautery cleaver.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
On the method of cauterization for pains due to injury or impact.
Chapter XLVIII
When, in certain parts, pain occurs due to injury or impact, and this pain persists for a long time and does not yield to treatment with medicines, then it should be cauterized with a point-burn.
And the cautery of every part should be according to its size, and its thinness or thickness, and its strength, and the position of the torsion, and the pain it causes.
If, therefore, it is healed from the first cauterization, that is good. If not: then repeat the cauterization on that same place.
Since these pains have the habit of shifting from one part to that which is nearest, in order to alleviate them, they must be transferred. Therefore, it is necessary to follow up on them with cauterization until the patient is healed.
On the method of cauterization for leprosy.
However, in lepromatous patients, cauterization should be applied with great care. And especially the type of leprosy, which occurs due to putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy; so when considering to cauterize it, be wary.
If leprosy is beginning to appear and you have treated it as we said before, but it does not disappear or recede, and you are afraid that the corruption has spread over the entire complexion of the body; then cauterize it on the head with five cauterizations: one in the middle of the forehead, and a second below it facing the front at the end of the hair, and two on either side over the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And finally, apply your hand with the cautery briefly, until it makes a slight impression on the bone, and the scales come loose from it; so that the expulsion of gross vapors is facilitated from it, and cauterize over it again with another cautery, as was previously done.
However, if leprosy is now scattered over the body and appears clearly manifest; then you should cauterize with these cauterizations we mentioned for the head, and another cautery over the ends of the nose, and two cauterizations over each cheekbone, and two over the spine of the neck, and six over the spine of the back, and one large over the hip bones, and one above it; also over both shoulders, two over each knee, two over the softness of his chest; and cauterize him all over the joints, from the joints of his fingers and toes; and cauterize over every heel of his feet, and the palms of his hands.
And be aware of the nerves that are above the back of the heel, so as not to burn them.
And sometimes a burn is made with a hot iron on the bone of the ribs, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the bone of the skull.
And know that the more you add to the burning, the greater is the healing, and the more it brings relief.
And know that the sick do not feel pain from the burn as the healthy do; for their body is already stunned.
And the burns should be of appropriate size and depth according to the members and joints; according to what has been mentioned regarding the types of instruments.
Then care for the burns with flour and herb paste with honey, and other treatments, until it is healed.
**On the Method of Burning in Stunning**
When a member is stunned and treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it does not heal, then burn that stunned member according to its size or its smallness.
And let your cauterization be done in such a way that it does not penetrate too deeply into the thickness of the skin. Then take care of it with ointment until it is healed.
And when it is cauterized to a state of numbness that occurs in the hand and foot, at the joints of the spine near the exit of the nerves that move that limb, then the numbness subsides.
Indeed, one should not attempt this unless they are wise in the anatomy of the body and the exit of nerves that move the limbs.
Chapter LI.
When Albucasis is outdated and does not offer anything new in the art of medicine, then cauterize over that cautery deeply, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color changes.
Then take care of it with flour of herbs, and lentils with rose oil, and arni leaves, and pigeon's blood, and vulture's blood: each should be in equal parts: mix all these together, and apply them to a cloth, and let them adhere to the place until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing a cancer.
When the cancer is just beginning and it itself can be stopped; then cauterize it with a hot iron in the shape of a circle around its circumference, as required.
However, it has been said that it should be cauterized with the last iron in the middle.
But I do not find that to be the case; for I fear it may ulcerate, and I have seen it happen several times.
And it is better that it should be cauterized around its circumference with a circle, as we said, or with many hot irons.
On the method of cauterizing an abscess.
When someone has an abscess that is delayed in ripening, due to its own excess or because of the weakness of old age, when it becomes thin and there is little blood, or due to time, and you wish to hasten the ripening of the abscess, then cauterize around its circumference with many small hot irons. Then, release her. It will also be hastened by the ripening of the fruit.
However, if you wish to make an incision in it with a cautery, then apply the fire of the cautery, which has this form.
And place this itself in the middle of the wound, until it penetrates the skin; and let the cautery follow from this, as the disease requires, so that the pure current is restored.
Then take care of it until it is healed.
§ In the manner of cauterization, in a mild corrosive.
Head (L II I)
A corrosive is nothing but corruption in a moving member, and it corrupts itself; just as fire consumes dry wood.
If therefore you see a corrosive in a place that can bear the fire of a cautery, then apply many cauteries with small and large cleavages, according to what is suitable for the place where the corrosive is.
Then cauterize it from all sides until the entire corruption is eliminated and nothing remains of it thoroughly.
Then leave it for three days, and place over the burnt areas finely crushed sulfur with oil, until all the scabs and every corruption are eradicated.
Next, treat it with ointments that nourish the flesh.
If therefore you see that after three days the flesh is born with a healthy newness in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cauterization over what remains from the corrupted places.
And the corrosive [disease] should be treated sometimes with acute medicine. Indeed, it [the healing process] arises at the place of cauterization.
However, cauterization with fire is more beneficial for the healing process: and indeed I have already said that cauterization should be done with acute medicine in certain cases; therefore, take it there when you need it.
§ Regarding the cauterization of claws and warts.
Chapter 50.
This affliction often occurs in the lower parts of the feet; it is a thick, putrid matter that damages the foot.
And indeed, there is cauterization in them according to two methods: cauterization with fire, and cauterization with hot water.
As for when using fire, it is similar to cauterizing with a heated pen, made of iron according to the quantity it contains of the claw from every side and is thin at the margins.
Then place the same fire above the claw. Then, with the hand covered in cautery, revolve it around the claw until the cauterization reaches the depth of the claw, and leave it for three days until it begins to emit pus. Then apply it with a paste made from crushed garlic mixed with salt, and leave the paste on top overnight. It will indeed be eradicated from its roots.
Then care for the place with a healing ointment made from meat until it is healed.
If they are not improved and often occur on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet, then apply cauterization to them with hot water. It is as if you take a small tube made of iron or steel or a feather from a bird, and place it over the claw or any other part. Next, insert a small amount of warm water into a tube. Hold your hand and twist it slightly with the pressure of your hand, so that the edge of the tube is pressed against the root of the nail, and the warm water reaches the depths, to the root of the nail, and the patient should wait for about an hour after the application of the hot water.
Then release it, for the nail is eradicated along with its roots.
Do this with each one, one after the other, until you have treated all that are present in the body.
Then take care of them after they have been eradicated, using what generates flesh from ointments.
§ On the method of cauterization in tremor.
When someone experiences tremor due to cold in a nerve, or from quartan fever, or any other cause, then they should be cauterized four or five times over the spinal bones, and between each spinal bone with a cautery, and also over the chest, and over the stomach.
For tremor ceases with the application of oil cauterization, and hastens the healing of cold disease.
On the manner of cauterization according to Albucasis.
Chapter LVII.
Sometimes Albucasis expels impurities from the body, that is, pustules that are formed from corrupted coarse materials.
Therefore, when you see them appearing, they should be cauterized with a fine iron on every part of the pustule's head, whose tip is heated with fire. Or with the root of long Aristolochia. Or with a semicircular iron.
And when they are cauterized, they draw out the impurity as it was first expelled in this manner, and they do not increase, but break up the surplus, making them well, and healing from them.
However, it should be done after evacuation with phlebotomy.
On the manner of cauterization in bleeding from an artery in the arm.
Many times there occurs a flow of blood from an artery that has been cut near a wound that happens externally or at the site of a scarification or cauterization of a limb, and similar things: and it becomes difficult to sever it.
Therefore, if this happens to someone, then apply with your hand directly to the opening of the artery, and place over it your index finger, and squeeze it tightly until the blood is obstructed under your finger and does not escape from it.
Then apply a small oil lamp and many more to the cauterization, and blow on them until they become very hot.
Then take one, or a few, or a large one, according to the wound and the place where the artery is severed, and place the cauterization on the same vessel, after which you move your finger quickly; and hold the cauterization until the blood stops.
If it is expelled with the withdrawal of the finger from the opening of the artery and the extinguishing of the cauterization, then quickly take another cauterization from those prepared in the fire.
Therefore do not stop doing this with one after another until the blood stops.
And be careful not to burn the nerves that are there, and let no further harm come to the patient.
And you should know that when blood flows from an artery, it is not possible to sever it; especially when the artery is large, unless with one of four methods. Or when using cauterization, as we have said. Or when using extraction, when it is not extracted. For when it is extracted, its ends are torn, and blood is severed. Or it is tied with a strong ligature thread. Or they place over it medicinal substances that aid in stopping the flow of blood, and tighten them with a suitable constricting bandage.
Whoever administers the severing with ligature and tightening with cloth, or positioning of burning substances and similar methods, does not do it thoroughly unless rarely.
If such a thing happens to someone and they have no doctor or medicine, then they should begin by positioning their index finger over the wound's artery opening as we described, and tightening it strongly until the blood is stopped from the upper part of the injury, and above the artery. And let not the finger be moved, but keep it always above the cold water, until the blood becomes congealed and swollen and can be cut off.
And meanwhile, consider what it needs from cauterization or medicine.
