Then clean it from all parts, as we told you in the extraction of the arteries in the temporal regions.
Then fasten it with a sharp knife where the double thread is located, and tie it itself at the first places where accidents occur; then tie it again at the last of them. Then cut it in the middle with a sharp knife along a straight line according to the length of the body, and extract what is aggregated from corrupt, foul humors.
Then treat the wound with the care given to the other wounds, where pus is generated, so that the muscles that nourish one testicle will fall away. It is not harmful through that.
However, if all the muscles become affected, then they should be extracted for this reason, so as not to be deprived of nourishment due to the incision, and it becomes weakened or withers and is not healthy with them.
Head XV.
On the care of intestinal ramified (or branched) structures.
The course of these ramified structures (or branches) is from a cut that occurs in the perineum over the urethra in the inguinal region near the entrails.
Why do the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles. And this rupture is either from a simple cut or from its extension.
And these two types occur for many reasons. Or from impact. Or through a jerk (or sudden movement). Or from noise (or commotion). Or from the elevation of a serious condition, and similar factors.
And the sign, when it is from the extension of a cut. It is that which happens gradually over a long period of time, and not suddenly; and the hernia is equal towards the deep side: for it compresses the intestines.
And the sign of its occurrence when it is from the section of the hernia, because it causes a sudden intense pain from the beginning; and the hernia is diverse, appearing under the skin nearby: and that is due to the exit of the intestine and its course towards the exterior of the hernia.
And when it emerges with the intestine, it is called the intestinal hernia, and the hernia; and sometimes it occurs with violence.
And sometimes feces run into the intestine and get stuck there, causing severe weakness; it causes intense pain, especially when pressed upon.
And in the treatment of these diseases, there is fear of complications; therefore, one must be cautious about such cases.
And the method of operation is to urge the patient gently to reduce the intestine by hand back into its proper position if he follows instructions. Then it should be raised above its collarbone between your hands, and support his legs.
Then extend the skin that follows the skin upwards, and dry the skin of the testes completely along its length. Next, fix two hooks of the section in the jaws, according as you need them to open the section with these: and the section should be according to the quantity that it is possible for it to emerge from.
Next, scrape the skin, and what is under the skin of the testicles, until the white siphon is detected, hard from all sides: then insert your index finger into that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white siphon, which is under the skin yes, and between the second siphon, and absolutely adhere to it with the adhesion which is in the posterior part yes.
Next, move with the right hand to the inner skin of the testicles: and with this, extend the white siphon upwards with the left hand: and lift the siphon towards the part of the section: and instruct the helper to extend the egg upward: and you dissolve the adhesion, which is behind by complete solution.
And ask your fingers not to be anything there from the internal untwisted into the white hard siphon. If, however, you find anything from it: then push it towards the middle below.
Next, take the thread, in which there is a thick filament, made licentious from ten threads: and insert it near the last siphon, that is, the tunic, which is under the skin of the testicles following the section: then cut the ends which emerge from the thread until there are four threads. Then he should compose some of them over others with a figure in the manner of a cross, and tie them with the same ligature as we mentioned, since it is firmly attached beneath the skin to the ligament of the testicles, until he can cause some of the substances that nourish them to be released towards them, so that nothing hot comes from there. And place another ligature again according to the outer ligature, distant from it less than two fingers. And after these two ligatures, release from the ligature, which is beneath the skin of the testicles, a quantity equal to the size of a finger, and cut off the remainder entirely according to its roundness, and remove it from there.
Then, cut, in the lower part of the skin of the testicles, a section from which the blood flows and pus is discharged, as we mentioned in what has been said above.
Then apply a bandage dipped in oil to the wound, and place it as we mentioned. And apply the ligature that we have described. And when the white ligature that we mentioned has been cauterized, after the incision of it, fearing the flow of blood. This often happens indeed. And release the ligature until it falls of itself.
If, however, the case is delayed, then it is bathed with hot water; and place on top of it what we have said, until it falls.
Then care for the wound with the rest of the wound treatment until it is cured.
Head XVI.
§ Of the Abundant Blood Vessel.
In this abundant vessel, one does not see anyone who dares to surpass its curative power with iron.
And indeed, they first said that it is done as we have narrated in the vessel which is with the vein. Which is, as you bind the vessels after cutting them with ease below; then dry in the middle, and treat afterward with what opens it, until the vessels fall; and care for the wound according to what we have said, until it is healed.
Head XVII.
§ On the Disruption Which Occurs in the Groin.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the opening protrudes, and nothing from the intestines descends below the scrotum; and if it does descend, it is but slight, and returns in all hours; but if it prolongs itself with this condition for some time, a fissure is added to the scrotum, until the intestines descend into the scrotum.
And it happened that this issue arises from the extension of the scrotum, which is in the groin, as we have said. For it extends the scrotum: then it becomes soft, and the space moves aside, and it protrudes.
And the treatment of it is with cauterization, as its preceding description has narrated.
And sometimes it is treated with iron, in this manner: and he lies down on his back between your hands. Then dry the place of the rupture that has moved aside and protrudes, by cutting along its width, according to the thickness of three fingers.
Then tie the scrotum and, what lies under the skin, until it detaches the white scrotum that lies beneath the skin which follows it.
Then take the radium and place it on top of the protruding place from the scrotum, and press it deep into the belly.
Then press upon the two protruding places at the ends of the radium from the scrotum, and sew one to the other; then extract the end of the radium.
And you should not make any incision with a knife at all, nor stretch or pull, as I have taught you in the treatment of intestinal branches.
Then turn your attention to the care of wounds. When, therefore, you make an incision with a knife, cleanse it, and heal the wound until it is consolidated.
Indeed, it contracts and does not add to the prominence of the rupture.
And cauterization is better at this site, for it is closer to health.
Head LXVIII.
§ On the softening of the skin of the testicles.
In some men, the skin of the testicles often softens because the flesh surrounding them becomes softened, and the appearance of it is disfigured.
Therefore, he who is charged with his care must make the patient lie on his back and cut all the softened skin that has become detached from the natural skin.
Then, aggregate the two lips with a suture. If necessary, use three or four sutures to soften the skin's excess and form a firm suture.
Then, make an incision between the sutures.
Then, take care of the healing of the remaining wounds until they are healed and the threads fall off.
Head LXIX.
**On castration.**
Know that castration is excommunicated by our law, and for that reason it is permissible for me not to mention it in this book of mine, and its remembrance is not necessary except for two reasons.
One of which is that it should be known by the doctor when asked about it, and that he should know its cure for whoever happens to have it.
And another reason is that we often need to perform castration on certain animals for our purposes, such as rams, wild boars, cats, and similar animals.
I say therefore that castration is done according to two methods. By friction. Or by cracking and cutting.
In cases where friction is used, the method of operation is as follows: We make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles become soft and relaxed and hang down; then we apply pressure with our hand until they break free and no longer appear under the touch.
In castration by cracking and cutting, you must hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the suspensory ligaments and dry the entire cut with a cloth, until two eggs have been laid; then, after you have cleaned them, make an incision in each one and do not leave anything remaining from the shell except a thin layer that is on the surface.
And this method of castration is better than that by friction, because friction may leave some remaining part of the testicles, which makes the animal desire copulation.
Then tend to the wound until it heals.
Chapter LXX.
§ On caring for hermaphrodites using both methods.
An hermaphrodite is found in men in two ways. One type is because it appears to have a space following it, or on the skin of the testicles, where there is a figure resembling a woman's vulva, with hair, and sometimes urine flows from that part on the skin of the testicles.
But in women there is one kind, which resembles a woman's vulva over the breast as if it were the pair of testicles in men, protruding towards the outside; of these, one is like the penis of a man, and two are like the two testicles.
And the treatment for these three types, two of men and one of women, is as follows: because it is necessary to cut into the added flesh until the impression of them escapes. Then, treat them with the same care as other wounds.
However, in the second type of men, from which urine exits on the skin of the testicles, there is no operation and indeed no treatment at all.
Chapter LXXI.
§ On the cutting of the tentigine and the protruding flesh on women's vulvas.
The tumor may be added to the natural one until it becomes inflamed and takes on an unsightly appearance, and in some women, it is so magnified that it expands like that of a man, reaching up to sexual intercourse.
Therefore, it is necessary that you hold the excess of the tumor with your hand or a hook and cut it, but not too close to the end, especially deep into the root, so as not to cause bleeding.
Then take care of the wound itself until it heals.
But when a tumor grows in the mother's womb, it fills itself until it reaches its full size, and sometimes it emerges to the outside like a tail, and for that reason some people call this disease "caudate" (tail-like). Therefore, we must cut it like we cut the tumor, and take care of it until it heals.
§ On the care of the Alratic (a rare condition in women not pierced).
Chapter LXXII.
Alratic is when there is an abnormal growth in a woman that is not pierced or has only a small opening. It is either natural or accidental.
Accidental is from a condition that precedes illness; it arises either from born flesh added, or by subtile and thin, or thick discharge, and occurs in the depths of the matrix, or on its sides, or on the upper or lower part of itself, and hinders coitus, impregnation, delivery, and perhaps menstruation.
Its recognition is done through the examination of obstetrics if pregnancy is evident and close at hand.
However, if it's not apparent, then seek it with your fingers or using a cane.
However, if the pregnancy is from a thin and subtle discharge and is close to two lips: then approach it and break it open.
And it is, as you place two little threads on the lips.
Then place your two hands together and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread apart. Then stretch the two lips with force until the thin discharge is broken and the pregnancy opens.
Then take a cloth, immerse it in oil, and place it on the spot; have the woman press it every day so that the place does not harden again.
If, however, the tumour is large and thick, then it should be cut out with a broad, similar spatula like a myrtle leaf.
If, however, the swelling is from flesh that has formed, then suspend it with hooks and cut it; and have with you medicines that stop the flow of blood without laceration, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and turpentine mixed with alum.
Next, insert a large lead pipe into the wound so that it does not heal quickly; hold it for several days. Then apply linseed oil, and afterwards continue with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
And when any new growths of flesh are born, then they should be cut according to this manner; for as long as there is no cancerous ulcer, which is the cancerous growth within the matrix, let there be no opposition with iron at all.
Head LXXIII.
**On the care of haemorrhoids, Atehelil, and bothor (rubella) in women's bodies.**
Haemorrhoids indeed are the opening of the veins, as long as much blood runs out of them persistently.
Since hemorrhoids have existed from ancient times, they are categorized into types and each has its own signs; I will discuss here which ones receive treatment and which ones do not.
I say, therefore, that hemorrhoids which are inside the anus and do not appear to the senses: then there is no treatment for them with a knife.
But those that are among them, on which the sense falls, are the ones that receive treatment.
Therefore, it is necessary that a woman should enter a cold house. Then she extends the hemorrhoids with forceps or with a rough cloth and cuts them off from their roots.
Then she cleans them near the flow of blood from one of the incisions without wounding: like myrrh, and dragon's blood, and pitch, and similar substances.
Then she pushes her feet against the wall at the same time. After that, she lays her down in cold water.
If the flow of blood persists: then make her sit in a decoction of sumac, and sweet almond peel, and gall, and similar substances.
Then take flour of barley and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on his back.
If blood comes out with it, that is good; and if not, make the plaster adhere to the back and the breasts without incision.
Then take wool and dip it in tar or sea-snail juice or grapevine juice, that is, in silver vitriol, wine, and make it adhere to the wound.
When the ulcer has healed, then take care of the place with ointments until it is cured.
Albucasis indeed describes the red bark as similar to the heads of almonds, and it has a rough appearance.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut what appears from it, as I said before, equally, and take care of itself until it heals.
Chapter LXXIV.
§ On the perforation of the matrix (ovary) which occurs.
Many kinds of ulcers occur in the matrix, such as cancer, stone ulcers, sores, abscesses, erysipelas, fistulas, hemorrhoids, cracks, and hot ulcers.
And I have indeed already spoken of all these diseases and the forms of them, and their signs, and their cures by division: it is necessary that I should speak in this treatise of the hot fistula that occurs in the matrix, when there are fistulas that gather up the blood, and to know how its opening is made with iron.
Therefore, it is necessary that you should consider. Then if the pain of the fistula is sharp in its beginning and accompanied by its inflammation and fever, and you see it turn red, and if the sensation passes over it, then you do not progress with its perforation; and treat it as it becomes better above the stage of maturation until such time as the acuteness of the accidents ceases.
Then you must make the woman sit on a seat that supports two cushions, and recline or lie down on her back, and bring her feet up to the lower part of her belly: and let her hips be spread apart, and place her arms under her knees, and bind them with the appropriate binding.
Then the midwife should sit on the woman's right side, and use the instrument to open the orifice of the matrix.
And when you wish to use this instrument, you must insert it into the deep part of the woman's matrix; so that what enters from the instrument does not exceed the depth of the matrix, and does not harm the sick person.
If the instrument is too long, then it is necessary to place small pieces on top of the cover of the deep matrix, in order to prevent the entire instrument from entering into the depth of the matrix; and it is necessary to place a guard, which runs along the side of the upper instrument, and to hold the instrument, and for the attendant to release the guard until the depth of the matrix is opened.
When the exit becomes apparent and is touched by the hand, and it is soft and flexible, then it is necessary to cut it off at its own head with a wide blade.
When the discharge is complete, then it is necessary to place on the wound a compress soaked in rose-colored oil or green oil, which has some astringent properties; and after placing the compress, extract the section into the depth of the matrix.
And place externally on the matrix, and over the comb, clean wool soaked in water with crushed stones.
Then, after two days, it should be treated with the appropriate ointment until it heals.
And when the matrix and wound are completely healed, then it should be washed with water and honey; afterwards, with water in which the root of lily or long aristolochia has been boiled, and finally return to the ointment.
If the wound is hidden inside the matrix, then it is necessary to prevent treatment with iron, and instead, take care of it as we said in division.
Chapter LXX: The Head
On Obstetrics: How embryos that have taken an unnatural form during their exit from the womb should be treated.
It is essential for an obstetrician to know the natural form of labor.
Therefore, from these signs, when you see a woman bending towards the lower parts and she desires fresh air, and relief is felt above her where the child is located, and it seems that the exit of the embryo is imminent; then know that this labor is according to a natural form, and the child emerges on its own head, and the second stage follows with it: either suspended or hanging from the umbilical cord.
When you observe these signs, then it is necessary to press her belly so that the embryo descends quickly.
For when it descends onto its own head, the second stage follows with it, and it is cleansed of those superfluities with a good cleansing.
However, if labor deviates from this form, it is unnatural and should be avoided.
For when the fetus emerges on its feet, and its body comes out before its head and feet, or one hand or foot at a time; or if its head and hand come out first; or if it comes out from inside; and perhaps turns around over its collarbone, then these forms are unwelcome.
Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be prudent and subtle in all these matters, and to guard herself against error and deception. And I will demonstrate all forms from them, and how the intellect is in each of them, and it shall be made known through that, and it will stand over it.
When the fetus emerges from its natural position above the mother's head, and it becomes difficult for her, and labor is now weakened in her, then make her sit on a seat or have women hold her; apply vapor to her private parts with cooked fennel and moist oils.
Then the midwife should insert her little finger into the vagina and find the second one with it, and cut it with her nail until what is inside due to moisture comes out; and press the woman's womb until the fetus descends.
If, however, it does not descend, then she should be enema-ized with the mucilage of fennel mixed with sesame oil.
Then after the enema, tell her to press herself; and make her sneeze with the condition, holding her jaw and nose at the same time. The fetus will indeed come out immediately.
If both hands of the fetus emerge first, then it is necessary to bring them down with ease gradually. If she does not obey at the entrance, then place the woman on a seat and raise her feet upwards; thereafter, strike the seat against the ground, and the woman must be held so that she does not fall during the striking.
If, however, the hands do not come out and the fetus dies, then cut them open and extract the remaining parts of the fetus; tie her hand with cloth and extract it with equal care, for it will come out.
The outcome of the embryo is on her feet. When the fetus comes out on its own feet, it should be gently pushed upwards; then, slowly turn the fetus around; afterward, leave it alone.
Then take one of her feet and slowly stretch it out.
When they come out as far as the thighs, then tell her to press and make her sneeze with the condition; for it will come out if God wishes.
And if it does not come out as we described, then slowly reduce the fetus until you place it according to its natural form. For it will itself come out then with easy exit.
If all that we have described is prohibited, then take some mucilage of aloe, and oil of sesame, and gum extracted; and grind it all well in a mortar with a good pounding. Then, with a line, mark the woman's vulva and the lower part of her abdomen. Then make her sit in warm water until she becomes relaxed.
When you see that her lower parts are heated up, then prepare a poultice of myrrh and apply it to herself. When she is holding the poultice for a suitable time, then make her sit on a seat. Then make her sneeze; and press her mouth and nose together, and gently press on the lower part of her abdomen. The heat will immediately come out.
The fetus emerges on the knees and hands. When the fetus is emerging in this manner, then carefully insert your hands one after the other. Then the woman should lie down on her back with her head raised and her feet hanging down; she should rest on the bed and interlace her hands. Then press above the wound gradually. Then extract what is beneath its feet from the particles, until it is prepared in the lower part. If the fetus does not emerge, then take its feet and move them with vigorous motion. Then press what is above the womb gradually, until the fetus ascends to the upper parts. Then he should insert his hand and take the fetus gradually, and especially instruct the woman to compress until the fetus emerges.
The fetus, hanging laterally from the hands. The hand should be manipulated for reduction. If, however, it cannot be reduced, then release the woman and make her walk.
If she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed, and shake her legs with violent concussion.
Then apply the liniment you prepared from mucilaginous substances.
If she has given birth, then make her sit on a seat. Then strive to reduce the hand and equalize the fetus according to its natural form: and make the woman sneeze, and strictly tell her to compress herself until it emerges.
When the fetus emerges over its own neck, with its hands expanded and its face toward the back of its mother. The midwife must hold the fetus' hand, then gradually unfold it and make it easy.
When it is equalized, then place on its head what we described above from oil and mucus.
Then tell her to move gradually. After you have done that, then make her sit on a seat and tell her to lean toward the right side. Then tell her to compress herself: and make her sneeze when ready.
The fetus' exit is prepared on the side. When it descends to the mother's opening in this manner with the secondine, then cut the secondine with your finger, until it is evacuated by moisture.
If it is hanging over the face of the fetus and its neck, then cut it from the umbilical area; so that it does not hang on and die.
Then push the fetus towards the inside until you place it as it should be, and tell the woman to press herself several times; for thus it will come out through the birth canal.
§ The delivery of twins or many fetuses. Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four are born. However, that of multiples is rare and occurs infrequently.
Indeed, it is a rare matter outside of nature, and they do not live completely; and [the mother] contains them, even if they multiply, in a single secondine; and they are separated through the sifach, distinguishing between each other what is tied together at the navel of each.
And when they come out, as a single fetus comes out through the natural birth canal easily; they come out through an admirable birth canal, as we have narrated.
If certain difficulties arise in their (the body's) treatment during childbirth and they reach what we have described from unnatural figures, then treat them as we have narrated: and let it be with fine care, doing what it does easily or slowly, and ingeniously according to every figure with whatever is prepared for it by ingenuity leading to health.
A reminder that it is formed in the womb from embryos, and some abort.
Sometimes one, and two, and three, and four, and five, and six, and seven, and more than ten are formed in the womb; and it has already happened to me that a woman, upon aborting, emitted seven, and others fifteen, all formed.
Which is measured by the glorious sage's art.
Therefore, all of this must be as it is in the knowledge of an obstetrician. Perhaps they may reach something similar to that; therefore, oppose it with what is necessary.
Chapter 76.
On the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you treat a dead fetus with what I mentioned in the process of division from medication, and it does not come out, and you take hold of it through an operation with the hand, then you must consider.
If therefore the woman is of healthy constitution and is not suffering from any of the accidents from which there is fear of her loss, then it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back over the bed, with her head inclined downwards and her legs raised: and let someone attend her from both sides, or bind her to the bed so that her body does not come out during the extraction of the fetus.
Then, moisten the mother's womb with moist oils mixed with alum, fennel, and flaxseed.
Then, the midwife should wet her hand with these oils and mucilages, and then insert it into the womb with ease. Then, she should seek with it the place where the hooks of the fetus are located, and the appropriate places for that.
Therefore, consider then if the fetus is prepared to descend over its own head: then fix the hooks in its eyes, or neck, or mouth, or in its palate, or under its beard, or in its chin, or in places close to its ribs, and under the ribcage.
If, however, the descent is above his feet, then it affects his chest and the middle ribs.
And it is necessary that he should hold the hook with his right hand, and place his left hand's pad on what is between the fingers of the left hand, and insert the hook with the hand easily, and fasten it in one of those places which we mentioned, until it reaches the empty space.
Then fasten another hook in opposition to it, or a third if needed, so that there is an equal contraction and it does not lean towards one side.
Then it should be extended equally, and not just in a straight line, but moved towards every part so that its opening is relieved, as is done with a tooth during extraction.
And it is necessary that in what is between them, the extension should be softened. If any part of it is retained, then the midwife should use some fingers with oil and insert them from the side to loosen what is retained.
If therefore the part of the fetus comes out, then the hooks should be moved to another place that is higher; do this until the whole fetus has come out.
If therefore the hand comes out before the others and it is not possible to reduce it because of its contraction, then it must be covered with a bandage. Then extract it until it comes out completely, cut it or make an incision at the joint of the foot, or the forearm; and so you must do the same for the other hand and both feet.
However, if the head of the fetus is large, or there is a contraction during its delivery, or water has accumulated at the top of it, then one must insert between the fingers the spiny Spatumile and catch the head with it and extract the water; or break it using an instrument called Almisdac, whose shape corresponds to that of the other instruments in the chapter that follows.
Similarly, if the nature of a large-headed fetus requires it, one must cut open the mother's abdomen; or extract the fetus using the Misdach, as we have said. Then, one should extract the bones with pincers.
Which, if the head comes out and is contracted near the fork, then it must be found until the humidity that is inside the chest is drained.
However, if it does not become complicated and does not obey to come out; then cut the head off as best you can.
If there is an abscess or hydrops in the lower abdomen, then it must be punctured until the humidity drains out of it.
If the fetus is indeed above its feet, then its attraction is easy and its direction towards the mother's mouth is lighter.
However, if it is compressed near the abdomen or chest, then you must extract it with the cloth that you have placed over your hand, and drain the abdomen or chest until the fluid drains out.
However, if the remaining limbs are removed and the head is brought back, then the midwife must insert her left hand. Therefore, if the mother's mouth is open, then she must insert her hand into the depths of the womb, and feel for the head with it, and draw it towards her with her fingers until it reaches the mother's mouth, after which she must insert one or two hooks and draw it with them.
If the mother's mouth is compressed due to the heat that has befallen her, then it is not necessary to struggle over it, but rather at that time she must administer the flow of humid substances, oily plasters, and sit in water that softens and moistens.
If the fetus is above its side, then it may be delivered, after which what we have said about a living fetus is administered.
If it is not possible to do that, then it should be cut off directly and extracted.
And it is necessary that you do not leave anything from the second part inside at all.
When you have completed your operation, then administer what I have said regarding the hot apoplexies that occur in the matrices.
If there is a flow of blood, then it should be stopped with a sting, and the remaining cure should be administered.
And indeed I have seen a woman whose womb was dead with a fetus within; then she became pregnant again over that same matter, after which the other fetus died as well. So it happened to her after a long time that an apoplexy occurred in her navel, and it swelled until it opened, and then began to discharge pus.
I was therefore called upon for her cure, and I treated her for a long time; but the wound did not heal.
I then placed some strong plasters on it; and the bone came out from its place. Then several days passed, and another bone came out. I am therefore amazed when there is no bone in the abdomen.
I therefore thought that they were from the bones of a dead fetus.
I then examined the wound and extracted many bones from a woman who was in better conditions; and now, after such a long time, it sends out only a little pus from its site.
And I did not confirm this foreign object here unless there is knowledge about it, and assistance to the skilled physician who treats with his hand.
Chapter LXXVII.
§ On the shapes of instruments necessary for extracting a fetus.
The form of the vertige through which the bone opens.
Here below is the shape of the stirrup, which equals the books, having two notches at both ends of two logs equal to each other. However, this notch should be more subtle in the stirrup, and it can be made from ebony or wood.
And the width of all the wood should be like two fingers; and each edge should be like one finger, and the length of each should be a palm and its midpoint; and in the middle of both woods are two additions of the same kind of wood, already fixed in both, whose length is the midpoint of a palm and a little more or less; and the width of each is like two fingers, or a little more or less.
And these two additions are inserted into the mother's bone so that it may open with them when you reverse the two vertiges.
The other form similar to it, more subtle and lighter.
Let it be made of ebony wood or brass according to the form of the pincers. However, at the end of it there are two additions as you can see above: and the length of each addition is about a palm, and the width of each is like two fingers.
When you see how to open the bone with it, then make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging down, opening what is between her legs. Then insert these two joined additions into the bone, and you hold the lower end of the instrument between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with scissors, equally according to the amount that you wish from opening the bone's mouth, until the midwife does what she wants.
The form of another vertigo than the ancients have named it The form that impels, by which the fetus is impelled.
The form of the almiscam, which counteracts the large head: and it resembles a fork, which has teeth at its extremity, as you see.
And sometimes it becomes obtuse, like a fork according to this form, as you see, which has teeth like saw teeth, with which it cuts and grinds.
The form of the near one who has a single spine.
The form of the near one who has two spines.
The form of the spatula with two ends to sever the head.
The form of two spatulas, also broad.
All these instruments are exercised, and the more kinds they have and prepared among artisans, the quicker their work is done, and the higher their reputation among men due to their quantity.
Do not therefore despise this instrument from them, but have it prepared for you. It is inexcusable, indeed, the need for them.
Head LXXVIII.
§ On the Extraction of the Second Tooth.
When the second tooth is retained at birth, then it is necessary that you expedite the weakening of the gum so that it retains its breath. Then make it sneeze when ready: and place your hand over its jaw, and its nostrils. If it therefore emerges through this, then it is good.
If it does not: then take a cup, and drill a hole in its lid: and put in it herbs that open the jaw, such as calament, rue, anise, chamomile, fennel, dill, and centaury: take all these herbs, or some of them, and steep them in water, and place them on the fire.
Then place a tourniquet of rush over the hole in the lid of the cup, and another end in the jaw: and hold it until steam reaches the depth of the mother's tooth.
Then make it sneeze as we said. The second one will then exit with ease.
However, if it remains after this treatment and does not exit, then instruct the midwife to immerse her hand in sesame oil or high-quality mucus. Then insert into the vagina and feel for the presence of the second one. When it finds it, then take it and gradually stretch it out.
If, however, it is attached deep within the mother's womb, then insert the hand as we described, until it finds the second one, and extract it gradually in a straight line, so that the womb does not fall during the powerful contraction; indeed, it must be turned to the right and left with ease. Then add to the amount of contraction. It will then obey and be held firm, and freed from adhesion.
Which if the womb's bone is constricted, as we have already mentioned, take care of it with sneezing and a poultice of herbs.
If, however, it does not emerge with all that we have mentioned, then be cautious not to tire yourself further by repeating the process of extraction.
Indeed, it is necessary that what emerges from the mother's womb be attached to the woman's hip. Then, apply a clister with a paste of four ingredients. Indeed, it will rot and dissolve after a few days, and then emerge.
However, when it rots, a bad smell is released from it that affects the stomach and head, and it harms the patient. Therefore, it is necessary that suitable fumes be administered to it.
Some of the ancient experts have already used nasturtium fumes and dried ficus.
The shape of the instrument used for fumigating a woman during childbearing and menstruation.
Make one from another material similar to the alcama or from bamboo: and place the broad end over the fire; and put the fumigation over the prunes; hold it until that fumigation is consumed; and repeat another.
**Chapter LXXIX**
On the healing of the unperforated gut.
Many children are born with unperforated intestines, which have already been cured by the subtle influence of sip (or perhaps a mild diuretic). Therefore, it is necessary that the midwife pierce it with her finger if it has not been done so already; and if not, she should pierce it herself with a sharp spatule, but be careful not to touch it.
Then place over it a cloth soaked in wine and oil. Then care for it with ointment until it is healed.
If, however, it is such that it becomes inflamed, then place a lead pipe in the wound for many days and remove it when the child wants to pass stool.
And it often happens that the gut becomes inflamed due to the healing of the wound or the abscess. Therefore, it is necessary that this consolidation be cut away, then it should be cared for as we have said regarding healing and lead.
Chapter LXXX.
On the treatment of fistulas occurring in the lower part.
Fistulas that occur in the lower part are either a protrusion or an enlargement that occurs near the anus, or they affect a single space and can be one fistula or multiple.
When that protrusion becomes hardened, it opens up, and moisture or thin pus flows from it.
And sometimes these fistulas penetrate through them. Therefore, they are recognized by what emerges from their discharge and the strength of the patient's defecation; and perhaps something escapes from them that is a worm.
And these fistulas are when they penetrate into the space up to the urethra and even up to the rectum. And these can penetrate up to the hip joint, and even up to the knot of the tail.
From what is recognized as a penetrating fistula up to the anus, even from one that is not penetrating, it is as if you insert your finger into the anus; and attempt to insert something thin into the fistula with air or iron: when there is no curvature.
If there is a twist in it, then insert into it a thin wire of lead or a hair from a horse's bristle, until you feel the wire, or a bristle on your finger.
If you do not feel it deeply, nor does anything come out of the wound in terms of discharge or swelling or pain as I have said; then know that it is not penetrating properly. So proceed towards cure accordingly.
And when the fistula penetrates to the urethra or to the bladder, then its meaning is that urine exits from it, and it prevents the place from healing with medicines.
If it is indeed penetrating to the hip joint or to the hip socket, then its sign is that the probe reaches there without any twist up to the hip socket, if there is no curvature up to the hip socket; and pain is felt around the part, and pus comes out of it always, and medicine does not heal it, nor does it solidify with ointment.
And in all these fistulas that penetrate, there is no cure at all; and their treatment is toil and vanity on the part of foolish physicians, who are built upon them.
But in those that are not penetrating and are not old, there is hope for healing with a splint; as I will tell you, and I have already tried it: and he should lie down between your hands on his back, and raise his legs up to his hips, and his hips should be inclined towards his breath. Then they insert a lead or air probe into the fistula's curvature, until you know where the attempt reaches.
If, however, the patient feels weakness around the anus, then you should insert your index finger into the anus.
If therefore you feel that your finger's attempt is already penetrating by itself, beyond what you feel between your finger and the anus or the flesh, then you know for certain that it is penetrating; so do not exert yourself on it, because its healing is not like we said.
They also said that in some men, the flesh heals and a cure is expected through medication, by gently applying hot cauterization according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before, and inserting the burning cautery into the fistula until it reaches around the anus. Then repeat this process twice or three times, until you know that all the added and filtered flesh is now charred, similar to a feather's thin tube.
Then apply the cure with lint soaked in butter until the charred flesh comes out, then apply it with ointments that nourish and solidify the skin.
If therefore it heals, it is good.
And if not, then it is never healed with any other treatment.
And if the attempt fails and it does not reach your finger which is inside, and there is a thick wall of flesh between it and the attempt, or if it is blocked: then you will see an opening in the skin following the course of the fistula, so dry the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and cut with the knife the attempt that is within the fistula, until the cutting reaches the end of the attempt where it becomes free, and it falls.
Then purify these filtered meats, which resemble thin feathers or ear canal hairs, so that nothing remains of them.
But if the blood binds you and releases you from the operation so that you can cut those meats, then it is better to cauterize with fire or with sharp medicine.
Because cautery with fire brings good habits to union, adds heat to those meats, and stops blood flow and dries up moisture.
Then care for it with lint wetted in butter or crushed garlic, until the place emits pus, and these burned meats emerge from the pus.
Then care for the wound with hardening ointments that generate hard flesh: and these are medicines which have stopping and drying properties.
For when you restore (the health), then it is already healed; and do not fear repetition.
However, if a fistula has already reached down to the depths of the anus and is extending due to excess fluid in the body; then insert your finger into the anus and examine it.
If therefore you feel a trial (or effort), and between you and it there is some pain or flesh that is close to penetration; then there is no operation on that part, unless according to your trust and hope.
Which is because it (the treatment) is administered in three ways: either by cauterizing it, as we have said; or by cutting it off, until you obtain its concavity, so that it becomes possible for you to insert a ligature and effect healing from thereon. And do not proceed too much with cutting, so as not to cut the fold containing the anus, and cause a hole to occur below without will (or control). Then take care of that as we said.
Perhaps it (the condition) will heal; or it will extend the fold, and clean itself after you dry it up close to the anus, as we said, either with a trial (effort) or with another sharp instrument. Next, cleanse the filtered meats that are in the incision until you can with scrutiny.
Then attempt the restoration of the wound throughout with the incision, and the upper hole where it is consolidated; and there remains a fistula open in the inner part of the anus, and it will be lighter on the inferior side.
And when a fistula occurs in this manner: and it is, when you insert a probe into the fistula: and it is on the side of the anus around the surface of the body with the skin and margin of the anus: then take the ends that are perforated, which is like a sharp needle, that is, the preparing coria, according to this form. And insert into it a threaded thread wrapped from five threads, and around that. Then insert a probe with a thread into the fistula until it reaches its depth.
If it is penetrating the inner margin of the anus, then extract the thread from that opening: so that you insert your finger into the anus and extract the end of the thread, and join both ends together: and tighten them both, and release it on one or two days: and as much as the thread penetrates the flesh, tighten it well until the meats between the two ends of the thread are cut through and fall off: then tend to the wound until it is consolidated and healed.
If, however, the fistula's opening is not penetrating: then make it penetrate in any way you prepare for it, unless it is located too deep. For it is not that you should not make it, but rather that you do not cut into the proper tissue because of a slip.
Then proceed as we said, until it is healed.
The shape of a spinous spatula that finds the fistula, whose curvature is sharp and acute, and its other part is not sharp so as not to cut what is unnecessary, as you can see.
Chapter LXXXI.
§ On the stitching of hemorrhoids, from which blood flows due to cutting them: and on the treatment of cracks.
There are hemorrhoids according to two modes. Either they are within the anus, similar to the seeds of figs or prunes; or as if they were new grains. And from them there are small and large ones; and blood flows from them always, and it is one but many. And they are outside and at the ends of the anus.
However, those that are outside the anus are, for the most part, of little humidity, from which citron water flows, or a slight continuous flow of blood; and they are according to the colour of the body.
And the treatment for what is inside the anus is, as you gently persuade the patient to defecate; and it is expressed until the anus is emptied, and appears healthy to you. Therefore, suspend them with hooks or hold them with your finger. Then cut them near their roots.
If, however, they do not retain hooks due to their humidity and the softening of both, then take them with a rough cloth or with thread from doubled linen, and extract them with your fingers. Then cut them, and after the cutting, apply some hot powdery substances to them to keep them in place at the site of the burn. Or, burn them according to what has previously been described in the chapter on burning. Then they should be cared for with the rest of the treatment until they are healed.
If the patient does not obey the evacuation of feces, then a weak enema should be administered to the patient in which there is a slight perforation, so that it may be relieved with what is present in the anus, and quickly obey the evacuation when the patient expels it.
However, if the external hemorrhoids are soft and easy to remove, then they should be taken with your finger or with a hook and cut off. Then they should be cared for with what we have said until they are healed.
And if one refuses to cut them with iron, then it is necessary to administer their stitching according to this manner. Take the soaked thread and insert it into the wound with precision. Then extract the hemorrhoid towards the upper parts and make it penetrate with the needle on its other side near the root; then soak both ends of the thread in the lower part of the needle and arrange them laterally, and tighten the hemorrhoid tightly with a strong grip. Then tie the thread and extract the needle.
Prepare that wound with all cleanliness and leave one part open so that excess blood can drain from it.
Then place a cloth soaked in pink or red oil over it and cover with another cloth; instruct the patient to rest. Then leave it until it falls off.
When the stitches fall off, treat them with ointment and continue the cure until they heal.
**On the treatment of fissures.** They often occur from constipation and the natural constriction of the intestines.
When they become ancient and medicine does not help: then you should use a knife or your finger to make them moist, until the upper layer of skin that prevents their healing is removed. Then care for them until they heal as necessary.
If they do not heal: then repeat the treatment with a stronger reason than before, until there is much bleeding and they are then cared for until they heal.
On the treatment of wounds, both open and closed, and of ulcers, and gangrenes.
**Chapter LXXXII**
You should know that an almirmar (abscess) is nothing but a round nodule according to the color of the skin, similar to the head of a nail; it occurs throughout the body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and fingers, and causes pain during walking.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut off what is around the nail's circumference and hold it with tweezers or a hook, and uproot it from its root.
Then take care of it, and if you wish to cauterize it, do so as mentioned in its preceding chapter.
However, from the gangrened (part) there is one small eminence, rough, filtered, round above the surface of the body. And this often happens in the hands of children.
And its treatment is to stretch the gangrened part, and cut into it; or tie it tightly with a silk thread; or with hair, until it falls off. And if you see it, cauterize it according to what has been mentioned, either with fire or with a sharp medicine; and now the diseased parts are eliminated, not those that are inverted with an instrument which I will mention.
However, the ant is also a small, filtered, thin excrescence on the surface of the body, penetrating deeply; and when it encounters cold, it feels like a bite from an ant, affecting the whole body, especially the hands.
And its treatment is to take a tube from the wing of a duck or a strong vulture's wing, and place it over the ant until it contains a circle of the tube's parts. Then, with your hand, turn the tube until you remove what is around the ant's circumference; and place it deep into the flesh, and eradicate the ant from its root.
And if you see it, make it with air or iron according to this form.
Place the upper part of the tube at the base to draw out a dead, wrapped-up obstruction so that it can be freed from your finger and its own twisting.
And if you see it, cauterize the ant according to what has been mentioned about cauterizing the diseased part as described in the chapter on cautery.
**Chapter LXXXIII**

Large clister.
