§ On the cutting of ends, and the locking of bones.
The ends putrefy, either from an external cause or an internal one.
Therefore, when you have treated the putrefaction with medicines, and it does not yield to treatment, and you see that the corruption occurs in a member, which does not affect anything else, then you should cut off that member where the corruption reaches, so that the sick may be saved from death or from the evil which is greater than the defect of the member.
And the sign of one who experiences this is that the member turns black until it can be attempted to be healed; either fire burned it or it putrefies after turning black: until that putrefaction extends to the rest of the body.
Therefore, with the appropriate incisions, and similarly if the cause of corruption is due to the impact of certain venoms: such as those of scorpions, jellyfish, and similar creatures.
If therefore the corruption or impact occurs in the extremity of a finger, then cut off the finger, and do not allow space for the corruption to spread, so that it may not extend to the rest of the hand.
And similarly if it occurs in the hand, then cut it off at the root of the forearm, and do not allow space for corruption until it takes hold in the forearm.
And if it suddenly occurs there, then cut off the arm at its joint near the elbow.
If however the corruption has spread, and you see it around the elbow, then there is mortal danger for the patient. And beyond that, care should be taken, for it is a matter of strength.
And similarly for the foot, when sudden corruption occurs in a toe, then cut it off at one of its joints; and if it takes hold in the toes of the foot, then cut off the entire foot. If it ascends to the knee, then cut the leg at the knee joint.
If the corruption has already reached above the knee, then there is no cure left other than to release it and leave the sickly one to die.
And the way to cut the member is either by severing it itself or by tying the ligature below, which you should cut, and tie another ligature above the place. And let the assistant stretch one ligature below, and let another assistant stretch a ligature above towards the upper part. And separate the flesh which is between the two ligaments, using a wide scalpel, until the whole flesh is detached. Then it is cut or tied.
And it is necessary that you put a linen cloth over all parts and do not allow the knife to touch the healthy place; and cause an addition of wound for the sick, and post-hemorrhage heat.
If, however, a flow of blood occurs internally while you are operating, then cauterize the place quickly; or put some powder over it that stops the blood. Then prepare for your treatment until it is completed.
Then bind the wounded member with an appropriate ligature and tend to it until it is healed.
And I tell you of what happened to a man on his foot, the same thing that I am telling you about.
That is, since it happened on his foot, there was a discoloration resembling the burning of fire, and that corruption first occurred in his finger, until the whole foot was affected.
The man therefore cut off his own foot after he saw the corruption affecting it with its intensity, which he found due to the pain, and the burning of it; and it was cut off near the joint, and he was healed.
And after a long time had passed, the same corruption occurred to him on his index finger of his hand.
He came to me, and I attempted to recover that superfluity with what I placed on his hand from medicines after purification of the body, but it did not cease, and it began to spread to another finger, until the corruption reached his hand.
He then called for me to cut off his hand, but he did not want it, hoping from me the reversal of that superfluity, and I feared even for his life if I cut off his hand. Since the virtue of man was superior to the case.
After he had despaired of me, he returned to his homeland and came to me because he had journeyed and had cut off his entire hand; and he was healed.
And I have not related this story except to serve as an aid regarding this condition of the illness and its genus; and so that it is clear, according to which action it is understood.
§ On the care of wounds and the quality of enemas with medicines.
When a fistula occurs in some fleshy members and the space of the fistula extends until it forms a collection of pus, then it ruptures or perforates, and what is within it from the pus comes out, leaving an empty place as if it were a cavity; and the skin over it becomes thin like a cloth that has been worn out; and it does not reach its final stage in corruption, nor does it affect the mouth, or the bones, or the ligaments. It deserves to be called a "sinus" and is not called a "fistula"; however, if the space of the fistula extends until the corruption affects any of these members, then it is called a "fistula" or an "abscess.
And the treatment is to cut that skin entirely as it has become hardened; and especially when it has become thin and like cloth, and you can be confident that it will not adhere to the place because of its corruption.
If, however, you hope that it will adhere to the skin and does not result in that final corruption from it, and if there is a thickening of the skin from flesh, then treat it with a clister; it is as if you were considering the sinus.
If it is large and the pus that comes out of it has a foul smell, then clean it with an Egyptian medicine, which consists of equal parts of vinegar, oil, and ziniar, and apply it over a fire until the medicine turns red, and it will thicken like honey.
Then take from it what is necessary and dissolve it in water and honey; use this to clean the sinus with a clister, tighten its opening, and leave the medicine inside for two hours.
Then extract it with expression; do this for several days until the sinus is purified and the foul odor is removed.
And when it is cleaned with a clister of ash water, if you do not have this medicine at hand, take ashes from burnt wood or from holly trees, and throw water over them. Then apply it and clean the sinus with it until you trust that the sinus is already cleansed.
If the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then clean it with a mixture of water and honey to which some crushed ziniar has been added. It cleanses itself with a mixture of honey and wine, because of the property of honey to purify and wash, and wine causes the wound to adhere, especially when there is an excess of cauterization and dryness in the wine.
You do this several times, and trust that the corruption of the wound has already been removed: then cleanse it with what causes new flesh to grow in it.
And it is necessary to take some dyafinicon paste and dissolve it in rose oil and astringent wine, or cleanse it with certain medicines and other ointments whose properties I have written about in the treatise on ointments.
If the opening of the wound is tight, through which a catheter for enema cannot pass, then widen it with a sharp iron, or put in it a moistened lint in Egyptian ointment, or in basilicon ointment, until it is widened.
And similarly, if the opening is also wide, then close its edges with stitching and allow the amount that enters for the enema to be without addition.
And similarly, if the opening from which pus flows is raised towards higher parts, then dry it in the lower location that is in it, so that pus can flow out of it to below: because when pus is constricted in the depth of the wound, it prevents new flesh from growing in it.
If it is not possible for you to cut the sinus around its lower part as you wish, then try to prepare the member in a way that allows the pus to flow out of it easily according to what you have prepared. Try not to retain any pus within it at all, and take the consolidative medicines that are placed on the wound, suitable for what you wish. And extend them over the linen cloth. And the cloth should be of such a size that it allows communication throughout the entire sinus. Then, use scissors to cut directly into the sinus's opening, enlarging it slightly more than the sinus's orifice. Then, extend another cloth with unguents over it, according to the size of the orifice, and place it above the first position far from the sinus's orifice, so that the pus can exit from it: and do not remove the large cloth for a few days, except once in a while.
The one who is over the sinus's orifice should be moved at all hours to allow what has accumulated in it from pus to drain out: and you must know if the flow of matter coming out of it is much or little: digested or undigested.
And consider again the place of the sinus itself; whether the lord of that part feels pain therein, or not; and whether there is a fistula there, or not.
And since your treatment is thus, and you see the matter that emerges from the opening of the sinus, then know that the sinus has adhered or approximated to the adhesion; then dissolve it in the morning, or on the third day; and when you have dissolved the ulcer, then change the bandage and renew the ointment.
But if a thin worm emerges from the sinus after a long space, then do not despair of its adhesion, for healing approaches it, since there are people who delay the regeneration of flesh in their wounds, and others who act contrary to it.
But if after many days a bad-smelling pus emerges from the sinus, then know that the sinus does not adhere.
If therefore the adhesion of the sinus is delayed, and its condition prolonged; then in the drying of the medicines, let the physicians make them such that they have humidity in their substance, and such dryness in their power as when added to it, excess of addition from moisture is removed.
And from the last part which is being cured, take dyafinicon ointment and dissolve it with pink oil, and apply it over it equal old wine in its substance.
Then make a wound in it with that, and use that very same thing.
And it does make a similar action to this one when you do not have the dyeing ointment at hand, honey, after you extract it, until it thickens, and use it. Or take myrrh, aloe, and incense; mix them all together, and sprinkle that over honey while it is still on the fire. Then cover it with a cloth and tie it over the wound; apply to that which you extracted from honey until it thickens, sprinkle on some powder, and place back over the cloth, tying it.
And when it is administered with long aristolochi, and roots of celestial lily, and becomes a lily; also flour of herb and centaury. Use them simple or combined, mix those, and sprinkle it over the honey I described; use that very same thing.
If the condition of the sinus persists and does not heal with this treatment, then know that there is corruption within it; or it already leaves an impression on bones, or on the hard parts of other members, or on ligaments; then treat it with the same care as fistulas, as mentioned above.
On the care of panary and inflamed nails, with the addition of a cut digit and amputation.
Panary is an abscess that forms under the thumb's nail, or any other toe nail; it may also form in the other fingers or toes.
When this condition persists and its treatment is neglected, the abscess becomes infected with heat or pus, damaging the root of the nail until it entirely decays, and the corruption may spread to the bone, causing a foul odor until the digit's end widens and turns black.
If, after treating it as we described above, your care does not improve, then you should cut off the entire remaining part of the nail with a knife. After that, cauterize the wound. Cauterization is indeed a powerful remedy.
If indeed the bone is healthy and the nail as well, and the nail's edges are pressing into the flesh towards the interior and beginning to hurt it, then you should place a thin piece of wood under the angle of the nail that is pressing on the flesh and push it up; cut off the flesh with ease, and put over it what remains of the flesh from burning medicines or decay, until it is entirely removed. Then, treat that wound with ointments until it heals.
However, if the corruption has already affected the mouth, then you must cut that mouth and extract the corrupted part: for it is never healed as long as the corrupted bone remains within.
If you see that the corruption and decay are spreading to the finger, then cut it off at a joint, as mentioned in the preceding reminder. Then treat the cut itself until it heals.
However, if the nail becomes damaged through friction or a blow, and there is severe pain, then it is necessary to use a leech to draw blood from the affected area first. Then dry the nail using a sharp spatula, cutting across it from top to bottom.
And be careful so that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail; for you cause severe pain to the affected area, and it will lead to additional inflammation at the site of the wound.
Then treat the area with something that alleviates pain.
The real digit that is found in some hands of men may be entirely fleshy; or perhaps there are bones within them, and possibly a nail on one of them; and some are born at the base of a joint, or their origin is in certain knots of the finger. Therefore, he who is born with certain finger nodes does not move, and he who is born near the joint of the finger perhaps moves.
Therefore, he who is among them is fleshy, his section (i.e., cutting) is easy. Which is, as you cut into the same near its root with a wide spatula.
However, the one whose birthplace is at the joint's root, its treatment (i.e., cure) is difficult. Therefore, abstain from cutting it.
In him who is born in a finger near the last node, then you should cut into his flesh first with a round incision up to the bone. Then saw the bone with one of their saws suitable for that. Then take care of it until it heals.
The healing that occurs in the fingers, moreover, often happens either from birth, meaning he is born with it, or from a wound's healing, or from fire burning, and similar things.
Therefore it is necessary that you remove that consolidation until the fingers return to their natural form. Then place between them a thin layer of lead or soaked cloth in pink oil; so that they do not adhere too quickly, and keep them apart. Or put between them a thin sheet of lead, until the place becomes consolidated as it should.
And similarly, if there is consolidation of some fingers with the palm, then dry that consolidation according to what has been prepared and it is appropriate for the shape of the member.
§ On the incision of a defect.
These are the veins that are involved in the circulation of melancholic humors, which occur in many parts of the body; and their flow is greatest in the legs, especially in those who walk or work, and bear heavy burdens.
Therefore, it is necessary that you administer an expulsion of the body from black cholera several times with strong expulsion.
Then the phlebotomist should draw blood from the veins of the patient.
The treatment of these veins, indeed, is according to two methods. One of them is that they should be cut, and black blood should be extracted. And another method is that the vein should be raised up, and all of it should be extracted.
The operation of it, indeed, is according to this method. It crushes the limb first with hot water greatly, until the thick, foul blood is resolved. Then it binds the limb of the patient from the upper part of the thigh to the lower part of the leg with a bandage. Then it cuts the vein at one, or two, or three wide sections.
Then it raises it up, that is, extracts the blood in your hand from the lower part of the leg upwards, and at the upper part it is necessary for the phlebotomist to cut the limb first. Then it cuts the skin down to below, until a quantity of blood sufficient and as tolerated by the patient's strength flows out.
Then bind it, and strictly order him to abstain from foods that generate black cholera, and repeat the evacuation and phlebotomy when veins are full, and hurt the patient.
The extraction of his tooth is done in this manner. If there are many hairs, cut the base of the nail carefully. Next, insert the whole (body) into a bath: or immerse a portion of it in hot water, until it turns red and the veins bulge; or subject it to vigorous exercise if there is no suitable bath available, until the member becomes heated.
Then dry the skin with a direct incision along the vein, or at its farthest end near the knee, or at the lower part of it near the ankle.
Then open the skin with forceps and scrape away the vein from all sides until it becomes visible; and at its appearance, you will see it turn red and then darken. When the vein is thus withdrawn from the skin, you will see it appear white like a string.
Then insert under it a forceps, until it is completely extracted and comes out of the skin; hang it gently with a blind hook.
Then dry another incision near it with three fingers. Then, scrape the skin from the upper part of the vein until it appears. Then handle it with the radii as you did before, and hang it up with another hook as you did initially.
Then dry another cut or multiple cuts if needed. Then raise it up and make an incision at the very last section near the heel.
Then extract it towards the section that is above it.
And do this until you have extracted it from the upper section or all higher sections, and when it comes out entirely, then make an incision on it.
If however, it does not obey you in being extracted and raised up, then insert a sharp two-edged blade and tie it, and extract it: or insert under it a radium, and twist your hand to every part until it comes out. And be careful, so that it does not get cut. For if it gets cut, then it will be difficult for you to extract it at all, and the injury will spread from that part.
After you have thus completely extracted it, place over the wound a bandage soaked in wine and rose oil, or just oil, and tend to it until it heals.
If the vein is contracted and has a twist that prevents its extension to the parts, and it is not as we said above according to rectitude, then you should find on it a place suitable for all its twists, and the places of its own extension.
Then suspend it with hooks until you have completely loosened it, and be careful near your incision not to pierce the vein or lacerate it, for it will be difficult for you to lift or extract it. Therefore, guard your prudence.
The shape of the incision that heals the vein.
The blind fold's shape.
It is not as hard as the rest of the veins, nor does it have sharp ends that could pierce a vein; instead, it has great flexibility, being soft. If it were thin, it would hurt the vein with its thinness, but on the contrary, it has superfluous thickness, as we said before.
On the extraction of the thigh vein.
This vein is generated in the legs in hot regions on earth, such as Alizegy and Arab land, and in dry, hot lands with little tenderness, that is, where grass or trees do not grow.
And perhaps it is generated in other parts of the body, except the legs.
And indeed, its generation is from the decay that occurs under the skin, as happens within the bodies of snakes and internal worms, and parasites generated between the skin and flesh.
And the sign of the beginning of the course of this vein is what happens in the leg with a burning inflammation. Then the site is used. Then the vein begins to exit from that site of use, as if it were the root of a plant or an animal.
When it appears from that end, then you must cover the entire segment with a lead fragment, whose weight is from one dram to two drams, and mark it; and let the lead be suspended from the leg.
Therefore, every time something emerges from it towards the outside, envelop that in lead and stain it. If it extends too much, then cut off that part and envelop the remainder. And do not cut it deeply until it has emerged completely. For if you cut it, it contracts and enters into the flesh, causing an ulcer to occur at that place, leading to putrefaction and a bad wound.
Therefore, it should be treated gently and extracted slowly until the last part emerges from it and nothing remains within the body; and from this vein indeed some men have a length of five palms and ten fingers. And now it has reached me, since a man has emerged from twenty palms (or inches).
However, if it is cut during your treatment time: then insert a knife into its hole and make a long wound with the body, until everything that is inside it of that material is emptied, and administer to the place of putrefaction with medicines for several days. Then take care with the same cure for ulcers.
And this vein, indeed, sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears at the ankle joint, or even in the foot itself; and it has numerous openings, and a branch emerges from each opening.
So treat it as we said in the division, and with what has been mentioned above.
¶ Regarding the section on worms generated under the skin, and it is said to be a "boil.
This boil is called a "boil" in some lands among us; because it often happens to cows, and is a small, thin worm that is born between the skin and flesh.
And it moves throughout the body, ascending and descending; and it is perceived by the sense as it moves from one part of the body to another until it breaks through wherever it breaks in the skin and emerges.
And its generation is from the putrefaction of certain humors. As worms and snakes occur, that is, roundworms (lumbrics) and tapeworms in the gut.
And he (the surgeon) fears harm from his evil intent. For when he (the surgeon) cuts into the body and it is carried to the head, and reaches a certain place, then perhaps he opens something within and comes out, and destroys the eye—and such happens often.
When therefore trying to cure it and extract the foreign body, then this happens only during its movement, and with the appearance of the object itself.
Therefore, it is necessary to tie what is above and below it with a strong strap. Then dry it above and extract it.
If it (the foreign body) is plunged into the flesh and you cannot find it, then place a caustic over the spot with fire until it dies.
And worse than that, is the corruption it causes, which corrupts the eye as we have said.
However, if you see it has already reached the head near the eye, then tighten a good strap under it. Then dry it above and extract it.
And it is necessary that the patient use purification of his body with medicines that dissolve bad, putrid humours.
And he should beware of foods that generate putrefaction within him.
§ On the section concerning the disease of Nakir.
This disease is called Nakir in our land: it is a pain that occurs in certain members, and then it changes from one member to another.
And I myself have already seen it, according to what I am telling you. I have been called to visit a sick woman in certain parts. And she withdrew her arm, and I saw a little swelling in the vein at the end of her arm.
And after staying for an hour, I saw one swelling move with a kind of pulse, as a vein moves, rising towards her shoulder more quickly than it can be perceived: like living silver running from place to place.
Therefore the pain has receded from that place and is fixed in the humerus.
Then, after a short time, it moves to the rest of the body, until it reaches the other arm.
He then told me that it was turning inside his whole body, as I could see.
I was amazed, therefore, at the speed of its change from one part to another. And I, indeed, had not seen before this affliction with my eyes in such a manner according to this way. However, I have seen many who find the pain changing from one part to another; and they do not see it with their eyes as they see it in a woman.
And I do not think that it is otherwise than because she was a woman of those who have such veins detected; from this, therefore, appears to the senses that change of wind has occurred.
And it is necessary that they do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate and humid bodies, secret veins.
If, therefore, you wish to cure it and the patient feels that pain, then if it appears before your eye, as we said, tighten over it, and under it, quickly; dry it above, until that vent is exhausted; and cauterize the place.
If, however, you do not see it with your eyes: then take care of it with the release of the body and with what it expels vapours, and cleanse them with foul pills, and pills of myrrh, and similar things.
**On the Extraction of Arrows**
Arrows differ according to their kinds, and according to the places where they fall from the body.
The diversity of these is indeed great, for some have large and sharp points, others small and blunted; some are concave, others convex. And among them are those that have three angles. And among them there are those with tongues (or blades). And among them there are those with stars (or points).
These are indeed those that are according to the members in which they fall, and they are according to two modes. For indeed the members are derived from principal members, such as the brain, and heart, and spleen, and lung, and kidney, and intestines, and similar organs. When therefore it falls upon any of these members, and you observe signs of death, which I am telling you afterwards, then you must endeavor to extract that arrow from them, for death follows him in which it is, in many dispositions. And when these signs of evil do not appear to you, and the arrow is not hidden deep within the member, then extract it, and tend to the wound.
Among the signs, when an arrow falls upon the brain and penetrates through the bone, emerging above it, it is: for from that there arise sudden vertigo, darkness, dizziness, redness in the eyes, swelling, redness of the tongue, spasms, confusion of mind, and choleraic deliria. And perhaps blood may emerge from the nose or ears. And perhaps speech is cut off, and the voice is destroyed. And from the wound's site, a white, pus-like moisture emerges. And from it, something similar to the moisture of the flesh emerges.
If these signs appear to you, then refrain from treatment and extract the arrow if it does not emerge.
The signs of the arrow when it enters the heart are: that it is near the left breast; and you feel it as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not in something hollow. And perhaps the arrow's motion is similar to the pulsation of a vein; and blood flows out from the wound, black. And this is followed by extreme coldness, cold sweat, and fainting. Therefore know that death descends without a doubt.
And the sign of the arrow when it strikes the lung is the discharge of foamy blood from the wound; and the limbs that follow, the neck becomes rigid, and the face turns pale. And the great, strong breath departs; and it seeks the attraction of cold air.
If an arrow falls into the chest, which is a small space, then it is near the ribs; and it causes great anxiety with intense pain and deep breathing, and all the limbs of the arms move.
And if an arrow falls into the stomach, then perhaps something undigested from the wound might escape through a side effect of food.
And if an arrow enters the abdomen and becomes lodged there: something of feces might escape from the wound, or a gallstone, or intestine that has already been ruptured. Therefore, there is no hope for its cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
If the arrow falls into the bladder and urine escapes from it: something flows out of it to the outside, and more intense pain occurs in the patient; then know that it is mortal.
The remaining members, such as the face, neck, throat, tongue, armpit, spine, pelvis, leg, and foot, and similar parts of the body are affected in many ways; when the arrow does not hit an artery or nerve, and is not a poisoned arrow.
And I tell you that I have seen these arrows to be used as signs for your treatment.
Which is because a certain man was struck by an arrow in his tear duct eye and at the root of his nose. I therefore extracted it from his other side, beneath the skin of his ear, and he was healed, without any harm coming to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from the Jew, which had struck him in the fat of his eye beneath his lower eyelid; and the arrow was already concealed, and I could only extract a small part of it, where it was embedded in his wood; and it was a large arrow, with a soft iron point, without wings.
The Jew was therefore healed, and no harm came to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from the throat of a Christian.
And it was an Arabian arrow, and it had wings. I therefore followed it up between the two ribs, and it was already submerged in his throat. I was therefore subtile in dealing with it until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
And I extracted another arrow that had pierced his abdomen; and we thought that he would die from it.
After thirty days had passed, there was no change in him regarding the arrow; so I took a different approach and extracted it, and he recovered, without any further complications.
And I also saw a man on whom an arrow had pierced his back, and the wound over it had healed. After seven years, the arrow came out at the root of his hip.
And I saw a woman on whom an arrow had pierced her abdomen; and the wound healed over it, and the arrow remained inside: and nothing changed from its position, and the woman did not experience any harm from any of her natural operations.
And I also saw another man on whom an arrow had pierced his face; and the wound healed, and remained, without causing him much pain, and there were many such cases.
And I extracted the arrow from a man at the king's court, which had pierced his nose in the middle, and was already declining to the right side a little; and the arrow was completely hidden.
I am called upon, therefore, to care for it after the arrow's wound for up to three days. I therefore find the wound of the arrow deeply strained.
I then examined it with a delicate touch and did not feel it; indeed, I found a puncture and pain beneath its golden right side. I therefore hoped that it was the puncture from the arrow's tip.
I then applied a poultice to the area, which had an attractive and soothing quality, confident that it would heal the place, and that I would see a sign of the arrow, so that I could cut it off above it; however, no incident occurred at the site, indicating that the arrow had not entered the wound.
I persevered with the poultice for many days; no incident occurred, and the wound gradually healed; however, it remained weak from the extraction for some time, until one day he felt the arrow inside his nose. And he told me that...
And he told me that... I then applied a sharp, corrosive medicine to the wound for many days, until it opened; and when I probed it with my finger, I felt the tip of the arrow that was adhering to the wood.
Then I added, in opening the wound, this sharp medicine, until the tip of the arrow became visible to us; and it took about four months for me to pass beyond that space with it.
Then, after the wound had widened, and it was possible for me to insert tweezers into it and move them around, it refused to yield and I had to continue working on it with subtlety and cunning until I began using properly crafted tweezers on a certain day, according to their shape at the end of the chapter, until I extracted it. Then I healed the wound.
And the doctors judge that the nasal cartilage does not heal. I therefore healed it, and the wound became consolidated and completely cured; not a trace of harm remained.
And I will tell you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you may establish a rule and meaning over what I have not mentioned.
Since the parts of this art and the distinctions between them are not comprehensible within the narrative; nor does the book understand it, and a prudent artist compares it with little over much; and with what is peaceful, he compares what is absent; and he finds a new operation and a new instrument among the descents of foreign objects in this art when they occur.
I say, therefore, that arrows do not exit from a member in which they are fixed, unless in two ways. Or through attraction from the place where it entered. Or conversely, of the other part.
And that which exits from where it entered, either it is an arrow proceeding into the fleshy part: it is attracted and exits.
Which if it does not obey to exit from the time in which it fell: then you need to let go of that for a few days, until the flesh around it putrefies: and its attraction will be released, and its exit.
And similarly, if it is fixed into a bone and does not obey you to exit, then let go of that for several days: and repeat the process with attraction and motion every day, until it exits.
If it does not obey you to exit after several days, then you need to drill around the arrow at every part of the bone with a fine chisel, until the arrows widen. Then attract it and extract it.
If, however, the arrow is already absorbed into the body and hidden from sight and sense, then seek it with the use of probes. If, however, you feel it, then pull it out with some instruments that are suitable for its attraction.
But if you cannot get above it due to the wound's constriction and due to the length of the arrow in deep places, and there is no bone, or nerve, or vessel there: then find a way above it until the wound becomes enlarged, and it becomes possible to extract the arrow.
If there are any parts that can be held, then free the fixed flesh from all sides, with every skill and device you have, until it is healed, without causing damage to the skin or deforming the ears.
And when you perform the extraction of an arrow, wherever it is located, then use a twisting motion with your hand, using pincers on all parts, until it glides out, and with the final subtle movement, do not break the arrow, making its attraction and removal for you difficult.
If you cannot remove it at once, then leave it for several days until what is around it putrefies. Then repeat the process. Indeed, it will be cured then if, against your expectations, a flow of blood occurs, then apply what we mentioned from treatment in its chapter: and protect your skill from cutting a vein, or nerve, or chord.
And use every skill possible to remove the arrow, and let it be with ease, or calmness, or slowness, or firmness, as I have told you.
And it is necessary that when you pull the arrow, it becomes weakened according to its form, as it was near the case of the arrow itself. Because it is more practical. If, however, it is not possible for you, then administer what is possible from the figures.
However, if an arrow emerges from the opposite side of a part or has already proceeded from it to external areas, the tip of the arrow forms a curvature at the end due to the sensation from the nearby skin's upper part, and you will see it protruding: so dry it above and make a cut according to the amount that the forceps can grasp.
Then pull it, for it becomes easier to leave on its own.
If it is indeed retained in the bone, then twist your hand according to the roundness until the arrow presses into the bone and increases its grip: then pull it out.
And if not: leave it for a few days, then repeat the process until it emerges.
If there is wood in the arrow, then push it along with that.
If, however, the wood falls and you want to apply pressure: then insert a sharp instrument into it so that its sharpness enters the arrow's tail: then push it along with that.
If, however, the arrow is bent, then push it with an instrument into that very place. For indeed, the arrow should be straightened through that.
If the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary to remove all the contaminated flesh, in which the venom resides, if that is possible for you. Then take care of it with whatever is appropriate for that.
If the arrow falls into the chest, or the abdomen, or the groin, or anywhere else that it is close to what you touch when you try to grasp it, and it is possible for you to cut across it: then cut, and cauterize the wound from the vein or nerve, and extract it.
Then dress the wound, if you see one, and take care of it until it heals.
And this is the form of pincers with which arrows are extracted.
The ends should resemble the shape of a hook, made like iron: when they grasp the arrow, they do not let go of it.
And they come in many shapes, large and small, and medium-sized, according to the amount of the arrow's length, its narrowness, the size of the wound, and its constriction.
The shape that impels (or encourages) the healing process.
And the shape that impels (or encourages) the healing of the deafness.
This is the extreme of deafness, as if it were a radius, so that its entrance into the hollow arrow (or cavity) may be relieved and compelled along with it.
§ On the letting of blood from veins.
The veins that are let with blood, whose custom runs through the body, are thirty.
Of which there are sixteen in the head: two pulsatile veins behind the ears, called the greater and lesser herbs; two arteries, visible on both sides of the temporal bones; two veins in each lacrimal bone of both eyes, called the attending veins; a vein prepared in the middle of the forehead; and a vein at the tip of the nose. And two guides, which are in the neck. And there are two veins that are in the upper lip of the mouth. And there are two veins that are in the lower lip. And these are the veins that are called Algocerich. And there are two veins that are under the tongue.
However, the veins that are bled in the arms, there are five veins in each arm.
One of them is called Cephalic, and it is on the outer side of the skeleton: and common people call it the vein of the head. And Fusca. And it is the middle vein, and it is composed of the branch of the basilic and the branch of the cephalic; and common people call it the body's vein. And Basilic, and it is situated on the inner side of the body; and it is also called Titillary. And common people call it the stomach's vein. And the ligature of the arm, and it is placed on the knife, and this is where the bleeding is stopped, and that which appears above the thumb by a clear indication.
And the little vein: it is the one between the ring finger and the little finger; and it has two branches.
And in the leg and foot, there are three veins. One of them is situated under the bend of the thumb, on the side of the sinew. And the second is the saphenous vein, and its location is near the heel on the outer side of the body. And the vein in the leg: its location is near the heel on the side of the sinew.
And in the leg, there are three other veins similar to these.
**On phlebotomy of two veins after the ear.**
True phlebotomy of the two veins after the ear, is indicated for ancient catarrhs, half-headaches, old wounds, and bad ulcers on the head.
And the quality of phlebotomy is what I describe. And it is done by shaving the head of the patient: and the nape of his neck is rubbed at the place of the two veins with a rough cloth, using good friction. Then the patient tightens his neck with a bandage, until two veins appear. And the places of them are behind the ears, at two depressed places of the head. Therefore seek them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse of them under your finger, there mark the signs with wax.
Then take the phlebotomy knife, and it is called the "Incidents. Then insert the blade under the vein into the skin, until the phlebotomy knife reaches the artery. Then raise your hand with the vein and skin towards the upper part, and cut the vein with the knife at the place of the incision made by the incident (cut). And the length of the cut should be the thickness of two joined fingers, or about that; and let it allow the blood to flow out as much as you wish.
Then tie it with threads and leave it until it heals.
And it has already preceded at the beginning of this book on incision and their sealing.
The two true arteries that are suitable for bloodletting at the two appropriate times for hemigrain are those of a strong and persistent headache, and excessive, sharp discharge around the eyes.
And the quality of bloodletting is as I have told you. The weak person should strain his neck much until two veins appear with a clear manifestation to the sense; and you should feel their pulse under your finger. Then indeed, the signs with encaustic.
Then lift the skin above the vein with your index finger, and insert the phlebotom (needle) from below, and then lift the vein to higher. And cut it, as you did with the other two veins; and let blood flow according to your need's quantity.
Then release the ligature at the lower end and place your finger on the vein just above the pulse. Next, place a bandage and little twine over the same spot and tie it tightly; then release it until the wound heals.
And now let us recall those things, the incisions, and their extraction as described at the beginning of this book.
The true instrument for venesection on the forehead is indeed used after cephalica venesection for ancient facial ailments, and for hemicranias, and redness, and foul ulcers.
And the quality of this venesection is, as I will tell you. The ligature tightens the patient's neck with a cut until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called the "fossor.
Place the sharp point that is at the top of the surgeon's knife over the vein itself, and strike it with a saw or any other instrument in such a way, and allow the blood to flow according to its quantity. Then, solve the lower perforation and tighten it until it heals.
And when it is opened with a phlebotome on its side. However, it is not necessary for the phlebotome to have a sharp point like other phlebotomes; on the contrary, it should have a wide end. And hold the phlebotome according to its reversal, since the wound is close, and perhaps the phlebotome will break when it is thin.
The instrument for the two veins that are in the two lacrimal ducts of the eyes is used for the eye due to itching and redness, and also for conditions in the eye and face.
And the quality of the phlebotomy of them is such that it tightens the weak neck with bloodletting. Then take the phlebotome and stand over his head.
And let the phlebotomy be done according to the transverse direction to a slight length with a small, slightly broad phlebotome, for in this place it is not expensive. For if the phlebotome is too thin at the end, it may perhaps break.
Then make it flow out of the blood as much as is necessary for you. And place a cloth over them, tighten them once at night, and loosen them.
The veins of the nose, indeed, when subjected to phlebotomy, are for acute fever, severe headaches, and facial pains, such as hemicranias, and the redness that occurs on the face, especially when it is long-standing.
And the quality of this phlebotomy is such that it tightens the patient's weak neck. Then hold the nose with your left hand, and take a thin, long phlebotome; fix it in the middle of its length, between what distinguishes the nose according to straightness. Since the vein is not visible to the senses there, and because blood begins to flow immediately.
And it is necessary that you finish with your hand the operation with a phlebotomist shortly, and make the blood flow as needed. Then bind it once during the night. For it is restored quickly.
According to the true Guide for phlebotomy, it (phlebotomy) is used for constricting anxiety, starting leprosy, melancholy disorders, impetigo and bad ulcers, and corroding, that is, worm infections.
And the quality of phlebotomy is such that it tightens the patient under both his chin with a bandage, and the artisan stands over the patient's head, and the patient sits on a seat.
Then the phlebotomist should make the vein wide for the phlebotomy shortly. Then extract from the blood an amount tempered or according to what you see is necessary for that. Then do likewise with another vessel.
Next, dissolve the ligature and tie two vessels with a medium tightness so as not to strain the weak one. And leave it until morning. Thus the wound heals.
§ On the bleeding of vessels, Albucasis. The method of phlebotomy for vessels, as Albucasis states, is as follows: because it leads to a buildup of blood in the mouth and gum corruption, bad ulcers, fissures of the lips, and even those in the nose and its surroundings.
And the quality of the phlebotomy is such that you should make the patient sit before you and tighten their collar with a cloth. Next, remove the patient's lips and look at two vessels, of which one is from the right side of the lip and the second from the left; their distinction is shown by the discoloration of the colors. And the truth is: because there are small, black vessels around them. Therefore, incise both sides with each other.
However, if doubt remains with you and you do not know which is the correct one, then turn to the larger of the incisions and those that are more obvious.
And similarly, do for the two veins that are in the upper lip; and indeed, custom usually follows this, so incise the two veins that are in the lower lip.
§ On phlebotomy: After the phlebotomy of the veins behind the head, treat the vein beneath the tongue. Indeed, the two veins that are beneath the tongue, when they are incised, provide relief for conditions in the throat, and the pain of the uvula, and disorders of the mouth.
And the quality of phlebotomy is such that the patient should sit between your hands in front of the sun; raise his tongue, and look beneath his tongue at one vein on one side and another vein on the other side; and the color of each will turn black.
Therefore, perform phlebotomy on both; and be careful not to use your last hand in performing the phlebotomy. For beneath them are arteries, and perhaps the flow of blood may occur from these arteries.
However, the three veins that are tapped in the forearm, namely the two principal veins and the vein located between them, are the ones on which blood-letting is customary practice for all people.
And blood-letting from them takes place according to two methods. Either by pricking with a myrtle-wood needle; or by using an olive-sized instrument to make it taper; or by cutting with a surgical knife, which is called Alnesil. And this is the form of it.
And from these there are various forms wide and thin according to the breadth and tightness of the veins. The form of the myrtle-wood needle's blood-letting is broad as you can see. And it is used to open veins that are concave, full, engorged, apparent, thick, and those containing thick, cloudy blood.
And this needle is of smaller breadth and more delicate tapering.
And it comes to the phlebotomy of the subtle veins that contain the subtle citrus blood.
However, the basilic vein, which is one of these three veins, has the most favorable (or powerful) phlebotomy point. Because it extracts blood from the ailments beneath the throat and neck, following towards the chest and vein; and the phlebotomist approaches it with caution, lest he be afraid of its artery that lies beneath it. So if he errs and adds to the phlebotomy point, he will hit that artery, and there will be a flow of blood. Therefore, it is necessary not to phlebotomize it with the phlebotomy instrument sharply; instead, it should be cut gently with an instrument such as a knife (or 'Alnesil').
If the basilic vein does not appear by its usual appearance, then you should look for another one and change to a different location, or seek out a branch of it; or phlebotomize in that place of the arm (the 'funem brachii'). Indeed, it (the basilic vein) is manifest, and it should be cut with the phlebotomy instrument (Anesil), as we said.
If you wish to perform phlebotomy on the same arm, then you must first relax the arm, so that you can feel the pulse until you know its location. Then mark the location with wax, after which relax the arm and use a concave-ended phlebotomizer as we described. And be careful not to strike the space around the artery's location.
And when you see that as you tighten the ligature, the swelling appears at the marked location with wax, then that swelling is due to the artery's inflation: so be swift in treating it.
If you see blood during phlebotomy that appears like a child's urine, thin and red, then know that it is from the artery's blood. Then act quickly, and place your finger on top of the long space, then remove your finger. If the blood is severed (it often severs multiple times), then tighten the arm and release it; and be careful that the patient does not move from fear: and place them above their fear.
And do not move it for several days until it heals.
If, however, blood does not stop flowing and seizes you, and you have no immediate remedy at hand, then cut the artery if it becomes apparent to you. For the extremities resist, and the blood flows out.
Or accept the fistula's skin and find its middle point, take one half, and tighten it over the vein with a ligature and a bit of thread until another day.
Then if the blood stops flowing, it is good. And if not: then attend to yourself with regard to the one whose memory precedes, from the place where the flow of blood from the wounds ceased: and the severing of his blood is not difficult in many dispositions, due to the small wound's location, and the possibility of binding it with a bandage from the arm.
The dark (or blue) veins, however, require a draw that extracts blood from the upper part of the head and the lower parts of the body; this is because it is composed of the branch of the Basilic vein and the branch of the Cephalic vein, as we have said.
And it happens that the phlebotomist should be such that there is no fear from the vein-letting, because under it is a nerve. If, therefore, he adds a phlebotomy puncture and discovers nerve vessels, there occurs in it stupor, and its healing becomes difficult, and perhaps it does not heal completely.
And this nerve often appears to the senses. However, if it is hidden in some people and is subtle, and it does not manifest: then you must place your phlebotomy where you make the phlebotomies, with the knife, and cut the vessels with the strength of your hand.
If the vein is between two nerves, then find the vein along its length.
**On the Cephalic Vein** However, the phlebotomy of the cephalic vein is beneficial because it draws blood from the head and conveys it to eye diseases.
And in this vein, if you wish, you must make phlebotomies by pricking it with a sharp phlebotomy tool, or with a myrtle phlebotomy: because it is the healthiest of all veins, since it is not beneath an artery, nor a nerve.
However, it is necessary for you, when making a phlebotomy, to take the head of the vein only with a phlebotomy tool, and seek a softer place, and it does not hurt him if it is not found with initial percussion, but rather turns over it with phlebotomy several times.
However, in some cases, it may be abandoned when, after the first blow, blood is not drawn from him, but that apostema does not harm him in any way.
§ On the usefulness of phlebotomy and precautions to be observed therein. The quality of phlebotomy and its accidents, on which one must ponder carefully for its rectification.
Firstly, it is necessary that you know that phlebotomy is not administered unless for the conservation of health and its continuation, and caution against the onset of illnesses.
And so that phlebotomy is performed on one of the three veins in the forearm, namely the cephalic, the femoral, and the basilic. And so that phlebotomy is performed at the beginning of the day, on an empty stomach, and in the springtime, summer, autumn, and winter after a meal when there are signs of overfullness.
And let phlebotomy be performed on the first day or third day after three hours have passed from the previous day.
However, phlebotomy administered for illnesses does not have a determined time; but when occasion and need call for it, it can be done at night or day, and at any hour or time.
And it is not necessary that boys be bled until they reach the age of fourteen years. Nor should a pregnant woman be bled until the fourth month until the seventh. Nor should the elderly, who have already passed sixty years, be bled.
So, if anyone wishes to be bled for any reason, he should cleanse his bowels before bleeding with a gentle enema, if much feces is retained in them; so that the veins do not draw harmful putrid excess from the intestines to the main members during bleeding.
Nor should a patient be bled when entirely sated from nausea or drunkenness until that condition is removed from them. Nor should an invalid be bled when suffering from hydrops.
And let bleeding be performed again after colic, vomiting, intestinal flux, frequent coitus, labor, exercise, vigils, fasting, and everything that dissolves strength from the body or animal.
Then consider the subtlety of the humors before that; if the blood is thick due to food, drink, and medicine: if possible, correct that.
Next enters the bath, if nothing prohibits it; otherwise, some exercise is performed to thin the blood.
And then perform phlebotomy on him in the chest around the third day, as we have said, and try to make his chest empty of all bad animal events such as distress, anger, fear, and also from all bodily events like labor, pain, excess, and similar ones.
And let him make his business present with those things of which custom has made use among people because of their pleasantness, scent, joy, and similar ones, in a quantity possible.
Then the phlebotomist should sit on a stool higher than the patient; then he should extract his arm and rub it with the phlebotomist's hand twice or three times. Then he should tighten the ligature with a strap and envelop it twice.
And the ligature should be firm but not excessive, because when the tightness is uneven or there is too much tension in the ligature, it hinders the flow of blood; conversely, if it is too loose, it also prevents the flow of blood.
After the ligature, the phlebotomist should then rub his hands together repeatedly until the veins swell and become visible to the senses.
Then the phlebotomist removes the blood with a small amount of oil, an ancient practice indeed.
Then he places his left hand's index finger on that vein in the place where he intends to make the cut, gently: so that the vein does not escape, and the blow is softened. Since the veins are like cords that escape during bloodletting, and among them there is one that flows with great force; and when you place the phlebotomist's tool on it, it contracts under the tool, deceiving the phlebotomist, and the phlebotomist does not open the vein properly; and if he does, it is tight. Therefore, for this reason, it is necessary that the phlebotomist be firm and careful in all these matters.
Then the phlebotomist should lay down. If the vein therefore opens at once with a single attempt, then it is good. And if not, then try again at that place a second time, gently or above the same spot with haste; if the place is not healed.
If the place heals or becomes weak, then release it on the day, or after two days; and do not tie the ligature tightly. Perhaps indeed the abscess draws in heat. Nor should the bath be entered.
Then he should perform bloodletting if necessary.
If the opening is small or the blood flows finely, be careful not to draw out more than is necessary; then repeat the phlebotomy in the same wound according to the right method and add only a little to the procedure.
And do this with haste before the place becomes an abscess, for the place that becomes abscessed is a small one in many people during surgery.
If therefore you see that the place has already become an abscess, then do not repeat over it at all, for nothing does it exempt itself from your attention. And place something of the dreg of oil over it, for it eases the flow of blood. And this is better in this place than the mere oil itself, and than all other oils.
And similarly apply the dreg of oil in all your phlebotomies, where you stop the flow of blood; and it makes a lard-like and wise substance when one of them is placed over that place.
Blood becomes thin and resolved when it is thick.
If, during phlebotomy, a great pus forms, which often happens, especially to those who are not used to phlebotomy, or there is only a small opening in the vein, then apply immediately and place over the spot a sponge soaked in hot water and salt; press it tightly for an hour, as it will resolve.
And it is necessary that you do that after the blood has left the vein, with its completion or from another vein.
If after a few days there remains at the site some blackness or purplish discoloration, it does no harm; and if you wish, place on it something of aloe or myrrh dissolved in water: or anything from the juice of mint, that is, menthol or something similar.
And indeed, many times abscesses and swellings occur during phlebotomy in the basilica.
Therefore, place your hand on that spot; if you feel any softness during your pressure on it, then that swelling is bad. So, put something on it from what we have said. For perhaps blood from the artery flows out of it.
But make a plaster for her with that which is there, where the constriction is, so that the place hardens. Then take care of it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
And it is necessary that you extract blood from every man according to the amount of his strength. And what appears from the color rising above the blood.
For if the blood is black, then let it be allowed to flow until it turns red; and similarly, if you see it thick, then let it flow until it thins out; and likewise, if it is sharp, then remove its sharpness until it becomes smooth.
And he who is full, strong, and needs blood extraction with one cut, should have the venipuncture performed on his side, and contrarily, for him who is weak.
And it is necessary to extract the blood from vessels, and that a tight opening be made; and better still is the administration of venipuncture, so that there is a crossed cut, not a puncture.
And this method of venipuncture is safe from the flow of blood and cutting of nerves; and it is more commendable and healthier than venipuncture by width and length.
And if anyone is accustomed to arrive at phlebotomy after a fainting spell, it is necessary that he should take some food before phlebotomy with a little bread soaked in grenadine water, or secaniabin, if heated; and draw blood from him in three or four places.
And if the complexion is chilled, then he should take some bread soaked in a mild syrup before phlebotomy, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, or in an aromatic scented syrup.
If a fainting spell occurs during phlebotomy and the cause is excessive blood loss, then he should take some meat broth and subtle aromatic syrup; and use aromatics with bandages, and press his chest with them; and employ the rest of what we mentioned in the division of fainting spells from evacuation.
Whoever wishes to restore his arm and drain his blood a second time: he who undergoes phlebotomy due to excessive evacuation and whose strength is weak, should drain his blood slowly according to his strength over several days.
Whoever truly wishes to restore his arm and drain his blood a second time, and he is physically strong: then he should do that after seven or nine hours, from the time of his first phlebotomy.
Whoever wishes to draw blood from his body to the opposite side from which it tends to flow: he should do that on the second or third day.
In a body where much blood has been already heated and heightened, it causes fever; it is necessary that blood be allowed to flow out in one stream, and a great quantity be extracted from it: the opening should be widened until syncope occurs; after you have preserved all conditions of phlebotomy, and place your hand over the pulse at the site where the blood flows, so as not to cause death by syncope. This often happens when the phlebotomist is ignorant, and it falls due to negligence.
And it is not necessary when you see the arm being released and the blood being discharged a second time, while the opening of the vein is already closed, and the exit of the blood becomes difficult, to press on it with force, lest the injured part be damaged or quickly extended. For that is a great evil; leave it alone until it has been bled a second time.
Or remove with care during phlebotomy that which has coagulated from blood in the vein opening, and place on it some dissolved salt in water. And place on it some of the paste made from alfalfa or sage, and apply gentle compression until the blood flows out.
If the vein has indeed burst, then leave it alone and do not press on it until the hematoma subsides.
If necessity arises to draw blood a second time and there is no excuse, then either perform phlebotomy on that very place or in another arm in another vein.
However, the phlebotomy site of the arm's veins is at the fusca (veins near the surface) and basilica (deeper veins), if they are not easily found and hidden because they are composed of them.
And the quality of this phlebotomy is that the patient should insert their hand into warm water until the blade turns red and the vein appears clearly.
Then it should be tied above that place with a ligature, applying a slight constriction. Then the phlebotomy should be made according to the crosswise direction gradually, not longitudinally or widthwise, and the opening should be wide, and your phlebotomy should be through that joint of the hand a little above.
If the exit of blood is blocked, then repeat immersing your hand in warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you achieve your necessity.
However, if it were the days of summer, then you should excuse yourself from immersing your hand in warm water. Indeed, the flow of blood into warm water is greatest in winter.
And phlebotomy of this vein is more salutary than any other vein, because it is not under this vein a pulsating or nerve vein.
True phlebotomy of the salutary right hand is conferring with liver diseases.
And the quality of this phlebotomy is such that you tighten the vein with your finger or hand, after you have inserted it into warm water, until the vein is bent and appears very much to the sense. Then the phlebotomist should cross it. And if you cut it completely, it will not harm that part in any way.

Then return your hand to the warm water and let the blood flow into it. For if you do not return it to warm water, the blood will clot in the vein's opening and be hindered from flowing.
After you have extracted the necessary amount of blood, then place on top of the wound oil and salt; so that it does not heal quickly.
And similarly, it is necessary that you do with every branch tightly.
The true instrument of this phlebotomy from his hand with the left is: because it is conveying to spleen diseases; and similarly do in his phlebotomy as you did in the second equally.
However, the instrument for phlebotomy of the saphenous vein is for diseases that are in the lower part of the body, such as diseases of the matrix, and retention of menstruation, and kidney ailments, and old ulcers of the coxa and crura, and similar diseases from others.
And the quality of this phlebotomy is that a weak foot should be inserted into hot water: and make friction over it until the veins swell; and tie above the joint of the foot with straps. And the veins indeed are located near the calcaneus, appearing towards the thumb; and many branches radiate from it on the face of the foot.
Therefore, make the phlebotomy on it in its wider branch, or near the calcaneus in its aggregate; because it is better and safer.
If the phlebotomist cuts it on the face of the foot, then be careful of the nerves that are beneath it and on the surface of the foot.
And place your phlebotomy tool across from the phlebotomist as if you wanted to cut it, and be careful not to harm the nerves.
However, if the outflow of blood is blocked, then immerse the foot in warm water and allow the blood to flow until it is completely drained.
If the phlebotomist mistakes the vein at first, then they should withdraw the phlebotomy tool slightly and move it higher up, since the area is healthy, and do not be afraid of harm from it when you are dealing with nerves, as we said.
And similarly with the saphenous vein of the other foot.
The sciatic vein, as we said, is located near the calf on the lateral side of the bone.
And the application of phlebotomy is to relieve the pain of the ankle, when it is due to hot blood.
